<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>The <b>Gaza Strip</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'z' in 'Zion'">z</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OED-Gaza_Strip_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-OED-Gaza_Strip-4">[4]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">قطاع غزة</span>‎‎ <i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="DIN 31635 Arabic">Qiṭāʿ Ġazzah</span></i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Arabic" title="Help:IPA for Arabic">[qɪˈtˤɑːʕ ˈɣazza]</a></span>), or simply <b>Gaza</b>, is a small self-governing Palestinian territory<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> on the eastern coast of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, that borders <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> on the southwest for 11 kilometers (6.8 mi) and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> on the east and north along a 51 km (32 mi) border. Gaza, together with the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>, comprise the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestinian territories</a> claimed by the Palestinians as the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">State of Palestine</a>. The territories of Gaza and the West Bank are separated from each other by Israeli territory. Both fall under the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian Authority</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> but Gaza has since June 2007 been governed by <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>, a Palestinian Islamic organization<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> which <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_legislative_election,_2006" title="Palestinian legislative election, 2006">came to power in free elections</a> in 2006. It has been placed under an Israeli and U.S.-led international economic and political boycott from that time onwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The territory is 41 kilometers (25 mi) long, and from 6 to 12 kilometers (3.7 to 7.5 mi) wide, with a total area of 365 square kilometers (141 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arnon_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arnon-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaza_Strip_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza_Strip-16">[16]</a></sup> With around 1.85 million <a href="/wiki/Palestinians" title="Palestinians">Palestinians</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pcbs_end_2015_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-pcbs_end_2015-3">[3]</a></sup> on some 362 square kilometers, Gaza ranks <a href="/wiki/Population_density#By_political_boundaries" title="Population density">as the 3rd most densely populated polity</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> An extensive Israeli buffer zone within the Strip renders much land off-limits to Gaza's Palestinians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Gaza has an annual population growth rate of 2.91% (2014 est.), the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_growth_rate" title="List of countries by population growth rate">13th highest</a> in the world, and is often referred to as overcrowded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaza_Strip_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza_Strip-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The population is expected to increase to 2.1 million in 2020. By that time, Gaza may be rendered unliveable, if present trends continue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unctad-2015_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-unctad-2015-21">[21]</a></sup> Due to the Israeli and Egyptian border closures and the Israeli sea and air blockade, the population is not free to leave or enter the Gaza Strip, nor allowed to freely import or export goods. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslim" title="Sunni Muslim">Sunni Muslims</a> make up the predominant part of the Palestinian population in the Gaza Strip.</p>
<p>Despite the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_Gaza" title="Israeli disengagement from Gaza">Israeli disengagement from Gaza</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-occ_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-occ-22">[22]</a></sup> the United Nations, international human rights organisations, and the majority of governments and legal commentators consider the territory to be still occupied by Israel, supported by additional restrictions placed on Gaza by Egypt. Israel maintains direct external control over Gaza and indirect control over life within Gaza: it controls Gaza's air and maritime space, and six of Gaza's seven land crossings. It reserves the right to enter Gaza at will with its military and maintains a no-go buffer zone within the Gaza territory. Gaza is dependent on Israel for its water, electricity, telecommunications, and other utilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-occ_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-occ-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>When Hamas won the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_legislative_election,_2006" title="Palestinian legislative election, 2006">Palestinian legislative election, 2006</a>, Fatah refused to join the proposed coalition, until a short-lived <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Unity_Government_of_March_2007" title="Palestinian National Unity Government of March 2007">unity government agreement</a> was brokered by <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>. When this collapsed under joint Israeli and United States pressure, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Government_of_June_2007" title="Palestinian Government of June 2007">the Palestinian Authority instituted a non-Hamas government in the West Bank</a> while Hamas <a href="/wiki/Hamas_government_of_June_2007" title="Hamas government of June 2007">formed a government on its own in Gaza</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deeb_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deeb-23">[23]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%932007_economic_sanctions_against_the_Palestinian_National_Authority" title="2006–2007 economic sanctions against the Palestinian National Authority">Further economic sanctions were imposed by Israel</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Quartet" title="European Quartet">European Quartet</a> against Hamas. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamas%27_takeover_of_Gaza" title="Hamas' takeover of Gaza">A brief civil war between the two groups had broken out in Gaza</a> when, apparently under a U.S.-backed plan, Fatah contested Hamas’s administration. Hamas emerged the victor and expelled Fatah-allied officials and members of the PA's security apparatus from the Strip,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> and has remained the sole governing power in Gaza since that date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deeb_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Deeb-23">[23]</a></sup></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Gaza" title="History of Gaza">History of Gaza</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rule_over_Gaza.2C_overview">Rule over Gaza, overview</span></h3>
<p>Gaza was part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, before it was occupied by the United Kingdom (1918-1948), Egypt (1948-1967), and then Israel, which in 1994 granted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority">Palestinian Authority</a> in Gaza limited self-governance through the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a>. Since 2007, the Gaza Strip has been <i>de facto</i> governed by <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>, which claims to represent the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian National Authority</a> and the Palestinian people.</p>
<p>The territory is still considered to be occupied by Israel by the United Nations, International human rights organisations, and the majority of governments and legal commentators, despite the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_Gaza" title="Israeli disengagement from Gaza">Israeli disengagement from Gaza</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-occ_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-occ-22">[22]</a></sup> and additional restrictions placed on Gaza by Egypt. Israel maintains direct external control over Gaza and indirect control over life within Gaza: it controls Gaza's air and maritime space, and six of Gaza's seven land crossings. It reserves the right to enter Gaza at will with its military and maintains a no-go buffer zone within the Gaza territory. Gaza is dependent on Israel for its water, electricity, telecommunications, and other utilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-occ_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-occ-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Gaza Strip acquired its current northern and eastern boundaries at the cessation of fighting in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1948_Arab-Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab-Israeli War">1948 war</a>, confirmed by the <a href="/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements" title="1949 Armistice Agreements">Israel–Egypt Armistice Agreement</a> on 24 February 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Article V of the Agreement declared that the demarcation line was not to be an international border. At first the Gaza Strip was officially administered by the <a href="/wiki/All-Palestine_Government" title="All-Palestine Government">All-Palestine Government</a>, established by the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> in September 1948. All-Palestine in the Gaza Strip was managed under the military authority of Egypt, functioning as a <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet state</a>, until it officially merged into the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Republic" title="United Arab Republic">United Arab Republic</a> and dissolved in 1959. From the time of the dissolution of the All-Palestine Government until 1967, the Gaza Strip was directly administered by an Egyptian military governor.</p>
<p>Israel captured the Gaza Strip from Egypt in the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a> in 1967. Pursuant to the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a> signed in 1993, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority">Palestinian Authority</a> became the administrative body that governed Palestinian population centers while Israel maintained control of the <a href="/wiki/Airspace" title="Airspace">airspace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Territorial_waters" title="Territorial waters">territorial waters</a> and border crossings with the exception of the land border with Egypt which is controlled by Egypt. In 2005, Israel withdrew from the Gaza Strip under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel%27s_unilateral_disengagement_plan" title="Israel's unilateral disengagement plan">their unilateral disengagement plan</a>.</p>
<p>In July 2007, after winning the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_legislative_election,_2006" title="Palestinian legislative election, 2006">2006 Palestinian legislative election</a>, Hamas became the elected government. In 2007, Hamas <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gaza_(2007)" title="Battle of Gaza (2007)">expelled</a> the rival party Fatah from Gaza. This broke the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_March_2007_National_Unity_Government" title="Palestinian March 2007 National Unity Government">Unity Government</a> between Gaza Strip and the West Bank, creating two separate governments for the Occupied Palestinian Territories.</p>
<p>In 2014, following <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamas%E2%80%93Fatah_Doha_agreement" title="Hamas–Fatah Doha agreement">reconciliation talks</a>, Hamas and Fatah formed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_government_of_2014" title="Palestinian government of 2014">Palestinian unity government</a> within the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> and Gaza. <a href="/wiki/Rami_Hamdallah" title="Rami Hamdallah">Rami Hamdallah</a> became the coalition's Prime Minister and has planned for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_general_election,_2014" title="Palestinian general election, 2014">elections</a> in Gaza and the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In July 2014, a set of lethal incidents between Hamas and Israel led to the <a href="/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="2014 Israel–Gaza conflict">2014 Israel–Gaza conflict</a>.</p>
<p>Following the takeover of Gaza by Hamas, the territory has been subjected to a blockade, maintained by Israel and Egypt,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESeib2012148_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESeib2012148-28">[28]</a></sup> with Israel arguing that it is necessary to impede Hamas from rearming and to restrict <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_rocket_attacks" title="Palestinian rocket attacks">Palestinian rocket attacks</a> and Egypt preventing Gaza residents from entering Egypt. The blockades by Israel and Egypt extends to drastic reductions in basic construction materials, medical supplies, and food stuffs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-middleeastmonitor2013_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-middleeastmonitor2013-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (August 2015)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaza.27s_Tunnel_Economy_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza.27s_Tunnel_Economy-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Under the blockade, Gaza is viewed by some critics as an "open-air prison",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-open-air_prison_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-open-air_prison-34">[34]</a></sup> although the claim is contested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prior_to_1923">Prior to 1923</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Gaza" title="History of Gaza">History of Gaza</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1923.E2.80.9348_British_rule">1923–48 British rule</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gaza_War_Cemetery_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gaza_War_Cemetery_3.jpg/220px-Gaza_War_Cemetery_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gaza_War_Cemetery_3.jpg/330px-Gaza_War_Cemetery_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gaza_War_Cemetery_3.jpg/440px-Gaza_War_Cemetery_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gaza_War_Cemetery_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_War_Graves_Commission" title="Commonwealth War Graves Commission">Gaza War Cemetery</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Palestine_Mandate" title="The Palestine Mandate">The Palestine Mandate</a> was based on the principles contained in Article 22 of the draft <a href="/wiki/Covenant_of_the_League_of_Nations" title="Covenant of the League of Nations">Covenant of the League of Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Remo_conference" title="San Remo conference">San Remo Resolution</a> of 25 April 1920 by the principal <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied and associated powers</a> after the First World War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cmd5479_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-cmd5479-36">[36]</a></sup> The mandate formalized <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> rule in the southern part of <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Syria" title="Ottoman Syria">Ottoman Syria</a> from 1923–1948.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1948_All-Palestine_government">1948 All-Palestine government</span></h3>
<p>On 22 September 1948, towards the end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1948_Arab-Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab-Israeli War">1948 Arab-Israeli War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/All-Palestine_Government" title="All-Palestine Government">All-Palestine Government</a> was proclaimed in the Egyptian-occupied Gaza City by the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>. It was conceived partly as an Arab League attempt to limit the influence of <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Transjordan</a> in Palestine. The All-Palestine Government was quickly recognized by six of the then seven members of the Arab League: <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>, but not by Transjordan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> It was not recognized by any country outside the Arab League.</p>
<p>After the cessation of hostilities, the <a href="/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements#With_Egypt" title="1949 Armistice Agreements">Israel-Egypt Armistice Agreement</a> of 24 February 1949 established the separation line between Egyptian and Israeli forces, and established what became the present boundary between the Gaza Strip and Israel. Both sides declared that the boundary was not an international border. The southern border with Egypt continued to be the international border which had been drawn in 1906 between the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Palestinians living in the Gaza Strip or Egypt were issued All-Palestine passports. Egypt did not offer them citizenship. From the end of 1949, they received aid directly from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Relief_and_Works_Agency_for_Palestine_Refugees_in_the_Near_East" title="United Nations Relief and Works Agency for Palestine Refugees in the Near East">UNRWA</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a> (1956), the Gaza Strip and the <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">Sinai Peninsula</a> were occupied by Israeli troops, who withdrew under international pressure. The government was accused of being little more than a façade for Egyptian control, with negligible independent funding or influence. It subsequently moved to <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a> and dissolved in 1959 by decree of Egyptian President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdul_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdul Nasser">Gamal Abdul Nasser</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1959.E2.80.9367_Egyptian_occupation">1959–67 Egyptian occupation</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Gaza_Strip_by_Egypt" title="Occupation of the Gaza Strip by Egypt">Occupation of the Gaza Strip by Egypt</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Che_Guevara_in_Gaza.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1078" data-file-width="1440" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Che_Guevara_in_Gaza.jpg/220px-Che_Guevara_in_Gaza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Che_Guevara_in_Gaza.jpg/330px-Che_Guevara_in_Gaza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Che_Guevara_in_Gaza.jpg/440px-Che_Guevara_in_Gaza.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Che_Guevara_in_Gaza.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Che Guevara</a> visiting Gaza in 1959</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the dissolution of the All-Palestine Government in 1959, under the excuse of pan-Arabism, Egypt continued to occupy the Gaza Strip until 1967. Egypt never annexed the Gaza Strip, but instead treated it as a controlled territory and administered it through a military governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The influx of over 200,000 refugees from former <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Mandatory Palestine</a>, roughly a quarter of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_refugee" title="Palestinian refugee">those who fled or were expelled from their homes</a> during, and in the aftermath of, the <a href="/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab–Israeli War">1948 Arab–Israeli War</a> into Gaza<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> resulted in a dramatic decrease in the standard of living. Because the Egyptian government restricted movement to and from the Gaza Strip, its inhabitants could not look elsewhere for gainful employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JB_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-JB-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1967_Israeli_occupation">1967 Israeli occupation</span></h3>
<p>In June 1967, during the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a>, Israel Defense Forces captured the Gaza Strip.</p>
<p>Subsequent to this military victory, Israel created the first settlement bloc in the Strip, <a href="/wiki/Gush_Katif" title="Gush Katif">Gush Katif</a>, in the southwest corner of the Strip near <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a> and the Egyptian border on a spot where a <a href="/wiki/Kfar_Darom" title="Kfar Darom">small kibbutz</a> had previously existed for 18 months between 1946-48.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In total, between 1967 and 2005, Israel established 21 settlements in Gaza, comprising 20% of the total territory.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1979_Israel-Egypt_Peace_Treaty">1979 Israel-Egypt Peace Treaty</span></h3>
<p>On March 26, 1979, Israel and Egypt signed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel-Egypt_Peace_Treaty" title="Israel-Egypt Peace Treaty">Israel-Egypt Peace Treaty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Among other things, the treaty provided for the withdrawal by Israel of its armed forces and civilians from the Sinai Peninsula, which Israel had captured during the Six-Day War. The Egyptians agreed to keep the Sinai Peninsula demilitarized. The final status of the Gaza Strip, and other relations between Israel and Palestinians, was not dealt with in the treaty. Egypt renounced all territorial claims to territory north of the international border. The Gaza Strip remained under Israeli military administration until 1994. During that time, the military was responsible for the maintenance of civil facilities and services.</p>
<p>After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian%E2%80%93Israeli_Peace_Treaty" title="Egyptian–Israeli Peace Treaty">Egyptian–Israeli Peace Treaty</a> 1979, a 100-meter-wide buffer zone between Gaza and Egypt known as the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphi_Route" title="Philadelphi Route">Philadelphi Route</a> was established. The international <a href="/wiki/Border" title="Border">border</a> along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philadelphi_corridor" title="Philadelphi corridor">Philadelphi corridor</a> between Egypt and the Gaza Strip is 7 miles (11 km) long. With the <a href="/wiki/Agreement_on_Movement_and_Access" title="Agreement on Movement and Access">Agreement on Movement and Access</a>, known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rafah_Agreement" title="Rafah Agreement">Rafah Agreement</a>, in 2005, Israel ended its presence in the Philadelphi Route and transferred responsibility for security arrangements to Egypt and the PA under the supervision of the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_army" title="Egyptian army">Egyptian army</a> has since destroyed some <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip_smuggling_tunnels" title="Gaza Strip smuggling tunnels">Gaza Strip smuggling tunnels</a> "in order to fight any element of terrorism", according to an Egyptian security official.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ma.27an_Aug_2012_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ma.27an_Aug_2012-45">[45]</a></sup> The Gaza border crossing into Egypt remains under the full control of Egypt. Egypt has alternately <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goods_allowed_or_banned_for_import_into_Gaza#Import_through_Egypt" title="Goods allowed or banned for import into Gaza">restricted or allowed goods</a> and people to cross that terrestrial border.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1994:_Gaza_under_Palestinian_Authority">1994: Gaza under Palestinian Authority</span></h3>
<p>In September 1992, Israeli Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Yitzhak Rabin">Yitzhak Rabin</a> told a delegation from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Institute_for_Near_East_Policy" title="Washington Institute for Near East Policy">Washington Institute for Near East Policy</a> "I would like Gaza to sink into the sea, but that won't happen, and a solution must be found."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 1994, following the Palestinian-Israeli agreements known as the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a>, a phased transfer of governmental authority to the Palestinians took place. Much of the Strip (except for the settlement blocs and military areas) came under Palestinian control. The Israeli forces left Gaza City and other urban areas, leaving the new Palestinian Authority to administer and police those areas. The Palestinian Authority, led by <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>, chose Gaza City as its first provincial headquarters. In September 1995, Israel and the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">PLO</a> signed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interim_Agreement_on_the_West_Bank_and_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Interim Agreement on the West Bank and the Gaza Strip">a second peace agreement</a>, extending the Palestinian Authority to most <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> towns.</p>
<p>Between 1994 and 1996, Israel built the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Gaza_Strip_barrier" title="Israeli Gaza Strip barrier">Israeli Gaza Strip barrier</a> to improve security in Israel. The barrier was largely torn down by Palestinians at the beginning of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Intifada" title="Al-Aqsa Intifada">Al-Aqsa Intifada</a> in September 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doron_Almog_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Doron_Almog-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:War_in_Gaza_023_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/War_in_Gaza_023_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/220px-War_in_Gaza_023_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/War_in_Gaza_023_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/330px-War_in_Gaza_023_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/War_in_Gaza_023_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/440px-War_in_Gaza_023_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:War_in_Gaza_023_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of Gaza in 2003.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000_Second_Intifada">2000 Second Intifada</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Second_Intifada" title="Second Intifada">Second Intifada</a> broke out in September 2000 with waves of protest, civil unrest and bombings against Israeli military and civilians, many of them perpetrated by suicide bombers. The Second Intifada also marked the beginning of rocket attacks and bombings of Israeli border localities by Palestinian guerrillas from Gaza Strip, especially by the <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Palestinian Islamic Jihad">Palestinian Islamic Jihad</a> movements.</p>
<p>Between December 2000 and June 2001, the barrier between Gaza and Israel was reconstructed. A barrier on the Gaza Strip-Egypt border was constructed starting in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anne_Barnard_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anne_Barnard-48">[48]</a></sup> The main crossing points are the northern <a href="/wiki/Erez_Crossing" title="Erez Crossing">Erez Crossing</a> into Israel and the southern <a href="/wiki/Rafah_Border_Crossing" title="Rafah Border Crossing">Rafah Crossing</a> into Egypt. The eastern <a href="/wiki/Karni_crossing" title="Karni crossing">Karni Crossing</a> used for cargo, closed down in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greg_Myre_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greg_Myre-49">[49]</a></sup> Israel controls the Gaza Strip's northern borders, as well as its territorial waters and airspace. Egypt controls Gaza Strip's southern border, under an agreement between it and Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-50">[50]</a></sup> Neither Israel or Egypt permits free travel from Gaza as both borders are heavily militarily fortified. "Egypt maintains a strict blockade on Gaza in order to isolate Hamas from Islamist insurgents in the Sinai."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005_Israel.27s_unilateral_disengagement">2005 Israel's unilateral disengagement</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_Gaza" title="Israeli disengagement from Gaza">Israeli disengagement from Gaza</a></div>
<p>In February 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Knesset" title="Knesset">Knesset</a> approved a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel%27s_unilateral_disengagement_plan" title="Israel's unilateral disengagement plan">unilateral disengagement plan</a> and began removing Israeli settlers from the Gaza Strip in 2005. All Israeli settlements in the Gaza Strip and the joint Israeli-Palestinian Erez Industrial Zone were dismantled, and 9,000 Israelis, most living in <a href="/wiki/Gush_Katif" title="Gush Katif">Gush Katif</a>, were forcibly evicted.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gaza_Strip_Barrier_near_the_Karni_Crossing.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Gaza_Strip_Barrier_near_the_Karni_Crossing.jpg/220px-Gaza_Strip_Barrier_near_the_Karni_Crossing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Gaza_Strip_Barrier_near_the_Karni_Crossing.jpg/330px-Gaza_Strip_Barrier_near_the_Karni_Crossing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Gaza_Strip_Barrier_near_the_Karni_Crossing.jpg/440px-Gaza_Strip_Barrier_near_the_Karni_Crossing.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gaza_Strip_Barrier_near_the_Karni_Crossing.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Barrier fence</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 12 September 2005, the Israeli cabinet formally declared an end to Israeli <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">military occupation</a> of the Gaza Strip.</p>
<p>"The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oslo_Agreement" title="Oslo Agreement">Oslo Agreements</a> gave Israel full control over Gaza's airspace, but established that the Palestinians could build an airport in the area..." and the disengagement plan states that: "Israel will hold sole control of Gaza <a href="/wiki/Airspace" title="Airspace">airspace</a> and will continue to carry out military activity in the waters of the Gaza Strip." "Therefore, Israel continues to maintain exclusive control of Gaza's airspace and the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_waters" title="Territorial waters">territorial waters</a>, just as it has since it occupied the Gaza Strip in 1967."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> has advised the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Human_Rights_Council" title="UN Human Rights Council">UN Human Rights Council</a> that it (and others) consider Israel to be the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occupying_power" title="Occupying power">occupying power</a> of the Gaza Strip because Israel controls Gaza Strip's <a href="/wiki/Airspace" title="Airspace">airspace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Territorial_waters" title="Territorial waters">territorial waters</a> and controls the movement of people or goods in or out of Gaza by air or sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isrlpa13698_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-isrlpa13698-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn2009-01-06_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn2009-01-06-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AI_briefing_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-AI_briefing-55">[55]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU" title="EU">EU</a> considers Gaza to be occupied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eccpalestine.org_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-eccpalestine.org-56">[56]</a></sup> Israel also withdrew from the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphi_Route" title="Philadelphi Route">Philadelphi Route</a>, a narrow strip of land adjacent to the border with Egypt, after Egypt agreed to secure its side of the border. Under the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a>, the Philadelphi Route was to remain under Israeli control to prevent the smuggling of weapons and people across the Egyptian border, but Egypt (under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU" title="EU">EU</a> supervision) committed itself to patrolling the area and preventing such incidents. Israel maintained control over the crossings in and out of Gaza, and the <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a> crossing between Egypt and Gaza was monitored by special surveillance cameras.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a> left the Gaza Strip on 1 September 2005 as part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel%27s_unilateral_disengagement_plan" title="Israel's unilateral disengagement plan">Israel's unilateral disengagement plan</a> and all Israeli citizens were evicted from the area. In November 2005, an "Agreement on Movement and Access" between Israel and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority">Palestinian Authority</a> was brokered by then US Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a> to improve Palestinian freedom of movement and economic activity in the Gaza Strip. Under its terms, the <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a> crossing with <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> was to be reopened, with transits monitored by the Palestinian National Authority and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. Only people with Palestinian ID, or foreign nationals, by exception, in certain categories, subject to Israeli oversight, were permitted to cross in and out. All goods, vehicles and trucks to and from Egypt passed through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kerem_Shalom_Crossing" title="Kerem Shalom Crossing">Kerem Shalom Crossing</a>, under full Israeli supervision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Goods were also permitted transit at the <a href="/wiki/Karni_crossing" title="Karni crossing">Karni crossing</a> in the north.</p>
<p>After the Israeli withdrawal in 2005 the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a> give the Palestinian Authority administrative authority in the Gaza Strip. The <a href="/wiki/Rafah_Border_Crossing" title="Rafah Border Crossing">Rafah Border Crossing</a> has been supervised by <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Border_Assistance_Mission_Rafah" title="European Union Border Assistance Mission Rafah">EU Border Assistance Mission Rafah</a> under an agreement finalized in November 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oslo_Accord" title="Oslo Accord">Oslo Accord</a> permits Israel to control the <a href="/wiki/Airspace" title="Airspace">airspace</a> and sea space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-2006_elections_violence">Post-2006 elections violence</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fatah%E2%80%93Hamas_conflict" title="Fatah–Hamas conflict">Fatah–Hamas conflict</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_legislative_election,_2006" title="Palestinian legislative election, 2006">Palestinian parliamentary elections</a> held on 25 January 2006, <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> won a plurality of 42.9% of the total vote and 74 out of 132 total seats (56%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> When Hamas assumed power the next month, Israel, the United States, the European Union, Russia and the United Nations demanded that Hamas accept all previous agreements, recognize Israel's right to exist, and renounce violence; when Hamas refused,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> they <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_economic_sanctions_against_the_Palestinian_National_Authority" title="2006–07 economic sanctions against the Palestinian National Authority">cut off direct aid to the Palestinian Authority</a>, although some aid money was redirected to humanitarian organizations not affiliated with the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The resulting political disorder and economic stagnation led to many Palestinians emigrating from the Gaza Strip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2007, fighting erupted between Hamas and <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a>. The deadliest clashes occurred in the northern Gaza Strip, where General Muhammed Gharib, a senior commander of the Fatah-dominated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preventive_Security_Force" title="Preventive Security Force">Preventive Security Force</a>, died when a rocket hit his home.</p>
<p>On 30 January 2007, a truce was negotiated between Fatah and Hamas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> However, after a few days, new fighting broke out. On 1 February, Hamas killed 6 people in an ambush on a Gaza convoy which delivered equipment for Abbas' <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Presidential_Guard" title="Palestinian Presidential Guard">Palestinian Presidential Guard</a>, according to diplomats, meant to counter smuggling of more powerful weapons into Gaza by Hamas for its fast-growing "Executive Force". According to Hamas, the deliveries to the Presidential Guard were intended to instigate sedition (against Hamas), while withholding money and assistance from the Palestinian people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Fatah fighters stormed a Hamas-affiliated university in the Gaza Strip. Officers from Abbas' presidential guard battled Hamas gunmen guarding the Hamas-led Interior Ministry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2007, new fighting broke out between the factions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Interior Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Talab_al-Qawasmi" title="Talab al-Qawasmi">Hani Qawasmi</a>, who had been considered a moderate civil servant acceptable to both factions, resigned due to what he termed harmful behavior by both sides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fighting spread in the Gaza Strip, with both factions attacking vehicles and facilities of the other side. Following a breakdown in an Egyptian-brokered truce, Israel launched an air strike which destroyed a building used by Hamas. Ongoing violence prompted fear that it could bring the end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_government_of_March_2007" title="Palestinian government of March 2007">Fatah-Hamas coalition government</a>, and possibly the end of the Palestinian authority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hamas spokesman <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moussa_Abu_Marzouk" title="Moussa Abu Marzouk">Moussa Abu Marzouk</a> blamed the conflict between Hamas and Fatah on Israel, stating that the constant pressure of economic sanctions resulted in the "real explosion."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Associated Press reporter Ibrahim Barzak wrote an eyewitness account stating: "Today I have seen people shot before my eyes, I heard the screams of terrified women and children in a burning building, and I argued with gunmen who wanted to take over my home. I have seen a lot in my years as a journalist in Gaza, but this is the worst it's been."</p>
<p>From 2006-2007 more than 600 Palestinians were killed in fighting between Hamas and Fatah.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)" title="Gaza War (2008–09)">Gaza War</a>, a series of violent acts killed 54 Palestinians, while hundreds have claimed they were tortured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> 349 Palestinians were killed in fighting between factions in 2007. 160 Palestinians killed each other in June alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007_Hamas_takeover">2007 Hamas takeover</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatah%E2%80%93Hamas_battle_in_Gaza" title="Fatah–Hamas battle in Gaza">Fatah–Hamas battle in Gaza</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Al_Deira_Hotel_Gaza_April_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Al_Deira_Hotel_Gaza_April_2009.jpg/220px-Al_Deira_Hotel_Gaza_April_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Al_Deira_Hotel_Gaza_April_2009.jpg/330px-Al_Deira_Hotel_Gaza_April_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Al_Deira_Hotel_Gaza_April_2009.jpg/440px-Al_Deira_Hotel_Gaza_April_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Al_Deira_Hotel_Gaza_April_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Al_Deira_Hotel" title="Al Deira Hotel">Al Deira Hotel</a> on the Gaza coast, 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the victory of Hamas in the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_legislative_election,_2006" title="Palestinian legislative election, 2006">2006 Palestinian legislative election</a>, Hamas and <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a> formed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_authority_national_unity_government" title="Palestinian authority national unity government">Palestinian authority national unity government</a> headed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ismail_Haniya" title="Ismail Haniya">Ismail Haniya</a>. Shortly after, Hamas took control of the Gaza Strip in the course of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gaza_(2007)" title="Battle of Gaza (2007)">Battle of Gaza</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-75">[75]</a></sup> seizing government institutions and replacing Fatah and other government officials with its own.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-intern_fight_p14-15_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-intern_fight_p14-15-76">[76]</a></sup> By 14 June, Hamas fully controlled the Gaza Strip. <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Palestinian_National_Authority" title="President of the Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a> responded by declaring a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a>, dissolving the unity government and forming a new government without Hamas participation. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preventive_Security_Service" title="Preventive Security Service">PNA security forces</a> in the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> arrested a number of Hamas members.</p>
<p>In late June 2008, Egypt, Saudi Arabia and Jordan declared the West Bank-based cabinet formed by Abbas as "the sole legitimate Palestinian government". Egypt moved its embassy from Gaza to the West Bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and Egypt supported reconciliation and a new unity government and pressed Abbas to start talks with Hamas. Abbas had always conditioned this on Hamas returning control of the Gaza Strip to the Palestinian Authority. Hamas visited a number of countries, including Russia, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> member states. Opposition parties and politicians called for a dialogue with Hamas as well as an end to the economic sanctions.</p>
<p>After the takeover, Israel and Egypt <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Blockade of the Gaza Strip">closed their border crossings with Gaza</a>. Palestinian sources reported that European Union monitors fled the <a href="/wiki/Rafah_Border_Crossing" title="Rafah Border Crossing">Rafah Border Crossing</a>, on the Gaza–Egypt border for fear of being kidnapped or harmed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EU_flee_Rafah_crossing_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-EU_flee_Rafah_crossing-78">[78]</a></sup> Arab foreign ministers and Palestinian officials presented a united front against control of the border by Hamas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abbas_wins_Egypt_backing_on_border_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Abbas_wins_Egypt_backing_on_border-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, Israeli and Egyptian security reports said that Hamas continued smuggling in large quantities of explosives and arms from Egypt through tunnels. Egyptian security forces uncovered 60 tunnels in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007_issues">2007 issues</span></h3>
<p>After Hamas' June win, it ousted Fatah-linked officials from positions of power and authority (such as government positions, security services, universities, newspapers, etc.) and strove to enforce law by progressively removing guns from the hands of peripheral militias, clans, and criminal groups, and gaining control of supply tunnels. According to <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, under Hamas rule, newspapers were closed down and journalists were harassed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AI_torn_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-AI_torn-81">[81]</a></sup> Fatah demonstrations were forbidden or suppressed, as in the case of a large demonstration on the anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>'s death, which resulted in the deaths of seven people, after protesters hurled stones at Hamas security forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hamas and other militant groups continued to fire Qassam rockets across the border into Israel. According to Israel, between the Hamas takeover and the end of January 2008, 697 rockets and 822 mortar bombs were fired at Israeli towns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In response, Israel targeted Qassam launchers and military targets and declared the Gaza Strip a hostile entity. In January 2008, Israel curtailed travel from Gaza, the entry of goods, and cut fuel supplies, resulting in power shortages. This brought charges that Israel was inflicting <a href="/wiki/Collective_punishment" title="Collective punishment">collective punishment</a> on the Gaza population, leading to international condemnation. Despite multiple reports from within the Strip that food and other essentials were in short supply,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Israel said that Gaza had enough food and energy supplies for weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Israeli government uses economic means to pressure Hamas. Among other things, it caused Israeli commercial enterprises like banks and fuel companies to stop doing business with the Gaza Strip. The role of private corporations in the relationship between Israel and the Gaza Strip is an issue that has not been extensively studied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to continued rocket attacks including 50 in one day, on March 2008, air strikes and ground incursions by the IDF led to the deaths of over 110 Palestinians and extensive damage to <a href="/wiki/Jabalia" title="Jabalia">Jabalia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Violence">Violence</span></h4>
<p>Violence against Christians was recorded. The owner of a Christian bookshop was abducted and murdered<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> and, on 15 February 2008, the Young Men's Christian Association (YMCA) library in Gaza City was bombed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Watchtower_rafah_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2242" data-file-width="3121" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Watchtower_rafah_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/220px-Watchtower_rafah_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Watchtower_rafah_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/330px-Watchtower_rafah_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Watchtower_rafah_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/440px-Watchtower_rafah_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Watchtower_rafah_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Watchtower on the border between <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a> and Egypt.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Egyptian_border_barrier_breach">Egyptian border barrier breach</span></h4>
<p>On 23 January 2008, after months of preparation during which the steel reinforcement of the border barrier was weakened,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breach_of_the_Gaza-Egypt_border_(2008)" title="Breach of the Gaza-Egypt border (2008)">Hamas destroyed several parts of the wall</a> dividing Gaza and Egypt in the town of <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a>. Hundreds of thousands of Gazans crossed the border into Egypt seeking food and supplies. Due to the crisis, Egyptian President <a href="/wiki/Hosni_Mubarak" title="Hosni Mubarak">Hosni Mubarak</a> ordered his troops to allow the Palestinians in but to verify that they did not bring weapons back across the border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Egypt arrested and later released several armed Hamas militants in the Sinai who presumably wanted to infiltrate into Israel. At the same time, Israel increased its state of alert along the length of the Israel-Egypt Sinai border, and warned its citizens to leave Sinai "without delay."</p>
<p>The EU Border Monitors initially monitored the border because Hamas guaranteed their safety, but they later fled. The Palestinian Authority demanded that Egypt deal only with the Authority in negotiations relating to borders. Israel eased restrictions on the delivery of goods and medical supplies but curtailed electricity by 5% in one of its ten lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The Rafah crossing remained closed into mid-February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2008, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_Israel-Gaza_conflict" title="2008 Israel-Gaza conflict">2008 Israel-Gaza conflict</a> intensified, with rockets launched at Israeli cities. Aggression by Hamas led to Israeli military action on 1 March 2008, resulting in over 110 Palestinians being killed according to BBC News, as well as 2 Israeli soldiers. Israeli human rights group <a href="/wiki/B%27Tselem" title="B'Tselem">B'Tselem</a> estimated that 45 of those killed were not involved in hostilities, and 15 were minors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>After a round of <a href="/wiki/Tit_for_tat" title="Tit for tat">tit-for-tat</a> arrests between Fatah and Hamas in the Gaza Strip and West Bank, the <a href="/wiki/Hilles_clan" title="Hilles clan">Hilles clan</a> from Gaza were relocated to <a href="/wiki/Jericho" title="Jericho">Jericho</a> on 4 August 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Retiring Prime Minister Ehud Olmert said on 11 November 2008, "The question is not whether there will be a confrontation, but when it will take place, under what circumstances, and who will control these circumstances, who will dictate them, and who will know to exploit the time from the beginning of the ceasefire until the moment of confrontation in the best possible way.” On 14 November 2008, Israel blockaded its border with Gaza after a five-month ceasefire broke down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> In 2013 Israel and Qatar brought Gaza’s lone power plant back to life for the first time in seven weeks, bringing relief to the Palestinian coastal enclave where a lack of cheap fuel has contributed to the overflow of raw sewage, 21-hour blackouts and flooding after a ferocious winter storm. "Palestinian officials said that a $10 million grant from Qatar was covering the cost of two weeks’ worth of industrial diesel that started entering Gaza by truckload from Israel."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 November 2008, Israel closed its cargo crossing with Gaza after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qassam_rockets" title="Qassam rockets">Qassam rockets</a> were fired into its territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> On 28 November, after a 24-hour period of quiet, the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">IDF</a> facilitated the transfer of over thirty truckloads of food, basic supplies and medicine into Gaza and transferred fuel to the area's main power plant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_Gaza_War">2008 Gaza War</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)" title="Gaza War (2008–09)">Gaza War (2008–09)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Damaged_housing_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Damaged_housing_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/220px-Damaged_housing_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Damaged_housing_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/330px-Damaged_housing_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Damaged_housing_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/440px-Damaged_housing_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
