</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="463" data-file-width="600" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008.png/220px-Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008.png/330px-Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008.png/440px-Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Israelis killed by Palestinians in Israel (<span style="color:blue;">blue</span>) and Palestinians killed by Israelis in Gaza (<span style="color:red;">red</span>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 27 December 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Israeli <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-16" title="F-16">F-16</a> fighters launched a series of air strikes against targets in Gaza following the breakdown of a temporary truce between Israel and Hamas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Israeli defense sources said that Defense Minister <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Barak" title="Ehud Barak">Ehud Barak</a> instructed the IDF to prepare for the operation six months before it began, using long-term planning and intelligence-gathering.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>Various sites that Israel claimed were being used as weapons depots were struck: police stations, schools, hospitals, UN warehouses, mosques, various Hamas government buildings and other buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Israel said that the attack was a response to Hamas rocket attacks on southern Israel, which totaled <a href="/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel,_2008" title="List of Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel, 2008">over 3,000 in 2008</a>, and which intensified during the few weeks preceding the operation. Israel advised people near military targets to leave before the attacks. Palestinian medical staff claimed at least 434 Palestinians were killed, and at least 2,800 wounded, consisting of many civilians and an unknown number of Hamas members, in the first five days of Israeli strikes on Gaza. The <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">IDF</a> denied that the majority of the dead were civilian. Israel began a ground invasion of the Gaza Strip on 3 January 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Israel rebuffed many cease-fire calls but later declared a cease fire although Hamas vowed to fight on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>A total of 1,100-1,400<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Palestinians (295-926 civilians) and 13 Israelis were killed in the 22-day war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>The conflict damaged or destroyed tens of thousands of homes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> 15 of Gaza’s 27 hospitals and 43 of its 110 primary health care facilities,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> 800 water wells,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> 186 greenhouses,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> and nearly all of its 10,000 family farms;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> leaving 50,000 homeless,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-114">[114]</a></sup> 400,000-500,000 without running water,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaza:_Humanitarian_situation_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza:_Humanitarian_situation-115">[115]</a></sup> one million without electricity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaza:_Humanitarian_situation_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza:_Humanitarian_situation-115">[115]</a></sup> and resulting in acute food shortages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The people of Gaza still suffer from the loss of these facilities and homes, especially since they have great challenges to rebuild them.</p>
<p>By February 2009, food availability returned to pre-war levels but a shortage of fresh produce was forecast due to damage sustained by the agricultural sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A_2014_unity_government_with_Fatah">A 2014 unity government with Fatah</span></h3>
<p>On 5 June 2014 Fatah signed a unity agreement with Hamas political party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc.com_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_Israel.E2.80.93Gaza_conflict">2014 Israel–Gaza conflict</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="2014 Israel–Gaza conflict">2014 Israel–Gaza conflict</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Connections_to_Sinai_insurgency">Connections to Sinai insurgency</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinai_Insurgency" title="Sinai Insurgency">Sinai Insurgency</a></div>
<p>Egypt's <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">Sinai Peninsula</a> borders the Gaza Strip and Israel. Its vast and desolate terrain has transformed it into a hotbed of illicit and militant activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationalpost1_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-nationalpost1-119">[119]</a></sup> Although most of the area's inhabitants are tribal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bedouins" title="Bedouins">Bedouins</a>, there has been a recent increase in al-Qaeda inspired global jihadi militant groups operating in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationalpost1_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-nationalpost1-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Out of the approximately 15 main militant groups operating in the Sinai desert, the most dominant and active militant groups have close relations with the Gaza Strip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timesofisrael1_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-timesofisrael1-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Egyptian authorities, the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Islam_(Gaza_Strip)" title="Army of Islam (Gaza Strip)">Army of Islam</a>, a U.S. designated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._State_Department_list_of_Foreign_Terrorist_Organizations" title="U.S. State Department list of Foreign Terrorist Organizations">"terrorist organization"</a> based in the Gaza Strip, is responsible for training and supplying many militant organizations and jihadist members in Sinai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timesofisrael1_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-timesofisrael1-121">[121]</a></sup> Mohammed Dormosh, the Army of Islam's leader, is known for his close relationships to the Hamas leadership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timesofisrael1_121-2"><a href="#cite_note-timesofisrael1-121">[121]</a></sup> Army of Islam smuggles members into the Gaza Strip for training, then returns them to the Sinai Peninsula to engage in militant and jihadist activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hamas_government">Hamas government</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Governance_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Governance of the Gaza Strip">Governance of the Gaza Strip</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamas_Government_of_2012" title="Hamas Government of 2012">Hamas Government of 2012</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UNSchool_DestrMoInterior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/UNSchool_DestrMoInterior.jpg/220px-UNSchool_DestrMoInterior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/UNSchool_DestrMoInterior.jpg/330px-UNSchool_DestrMoInterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/UNSchool_DestrMoInterior.jpg/440px-UNSchool_DestrMoInterior.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UNSchool_DestrMoInterior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damaged UN school and remmants of the Ministry of Interior in Gaza City, December 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Hamas government of 2012 was the second Palestinian <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>-dominated government, ruling over the <a href="/wiki/Governance_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Governance of the Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>, since the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gaza_(2007)" title="Battle of Gaza (2007)">split</a> of the Palestinian National Authority in 2007. It was announced in early September 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hurriyet0209_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-hurriyet0209-123">[123]</a></sup> The reshuffle of the previous government was approved by Gaza-based Hamas MPs from the Palestinian Legislative Council (PLC) or parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hurriyet0209_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-hurriyet0209-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_political_and_militant_groups_in_Gaza">Other political and militant groups in Gaza</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Jihad_Movement_in_Palestine" title="Islamic Jihad Movement in Palestine">Islamic Jihad Movement in Palestine</a>, also known as the Palestinian Islamic Jihad (PIJ) is a Palestinian militant organization operating in the West Bank and Gaza Strip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WIIJ_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-WIIJ-124">[124]</a></sup> The group has been labelled as a terrorist group by the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> the European Union,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> the United Kingdom,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Japan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Canada,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Australia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> and Israel. Iran is a major financial supporter of the PIJ.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Islamic Jihad is the second largest militant Islamic group in Gaza with 8,000 fighters present in the Gaza strip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IslamicJihad_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-IslamicJihad-133">[133]</a></sup> In June 2013, the Islamic Jihad broke ties with Hamas leaders after Hamas police fatally shot the commander of Islamic Jihad's military wing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IslamicJihad_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-IslamicJihad-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deal_with_Fatah">Deal with Fatah</span></h3>
<p>On September 25, 2014, Hamas agreed to let the Palestinian Authority resume control over the Gaza Strip and its border crossings with Egypt and Israel.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Status">Status</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_occupation">Military occupation</span></h3>
<p>The international community regards all of the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestinian territories</a> including Gaza as occupied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aj_reality_check_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-aj_reality_check-134">[134]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> has declared at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Human_Rights_Council" title="UN Human Rights Council">UN Human Rights Council</a> that it views Israel as a <i>de facto</i> occupying power in the Gaza Strip, even though Israel has no military or other presence, because the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oslo_Accord" title="Oslo Accord">Oslo Accord</a> authorizes Israel to control the <a href="/wiki/Airspace" title="Airspace">airspace</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territorial_sea" title="Territorial sea">territorial sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isrlpa13698_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-isrlpa13698-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn2009-01-06_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn2009-01-06-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AI_briefing_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-AI_briefing-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his statement on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="2008–2009 Israel–Gaza conflict">2008–2009 Israel–Gaza conflict</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_A._Falk" title="Richard A. Falk">Richard Falk</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Rapporteur" title="United Nations Special Rapporteur">United Nations Special Rapporteur</a> wrote that <a href="/wiki/International_humanitarian_law" title="International humanitarian law">international humanitarian law</a> applied to Israel "in regard to the obligations of an Occupying Power and in the requirements of the laws of war."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_United_Nations" title="The United Nations">The United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Fact_Finding_Mission_on_the_2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="United Nations Fact Finding Mission on the 2014 Israel–Gaza conflict">UN Fact Finding Mission to Gaza</a>, international human rights organizations, US government websites, the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">UK Foreign and Commonwealth Office</a>, and a significant number of legal commentators (<a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Aronson" title="Geoffrey Aronson">Geoffrey Aronson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meron_Benvenisti" title="Meron Benvenisti">Meron Benvenisti</a>, Claude Bruderlein, Sari Bashi and Kenneth Mann, Shane Darcy and John Reynolds, <a href="/wiki/Yoram_Dinstein" title="Yoram Dinstein">Yoram Dinstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Dugard" title="John Dugard">John Dugard</a>, Marc S. Kaliser, <a href="/wiki/Birzeit_University" title="Birzeit University">Mustafa Mari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iain_Scobbie" title="Iain Scobbie">Iain Scobbie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Israel_Law_Review" title="Israel Law Review">Yuval Shany</a> maintain that Israel's extensive direct external control over Gaza, and indirect control over the lives of its internal population mean that Gaza remained occupied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>Israel states that it does not exercise effective control or authority over any land or institutions in the Gaza Strip and thus the Gaza Strip is no longer subject to the former <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">military occupation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gold_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gold-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_Affairs_Minister_of_Israel" title="Foreign Affairs Minister of Israel">Foreign Affairs Minister of Israel</a> <a href="/wiki/Tzipi_Livni" title="Tzipi Livni">Tzipi Livni</a> stated in January 2008: "Israel got out of Gaza. It dismantled its settlements there. No Israeli soldiers were left there after the disengagement."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> In spite of <a href="/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_Gaza" title="Israeli disengagement from Gaza">Israel's withdrawal from Gaza in 2005</a>, the Hamas Government in Gaza considers Gaza as occupied territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hamas_faq_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-hamas_faq-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Control_over_airspace">Control over airspace</span></h3>
<p>As agreed between Israel and the Palestinian Authority in the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a>, Israel has exclusive control over the airspace. It can interfere with radio and TV transmissions, and the Palestinian Authority cannot engage in independent initiatives for operating a seaport or airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> The Accords also permitted Palestinians to construct an airport, which was duly built and opened in 1998. Israel destroyed Gaza's only airport in 2001 and 2002, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Intifada" title="Second Intifada">Second Intifada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc_fly_again_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc_fly_again-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc2005_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2005-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Israeli army makes use of <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_combat_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned combat aerial vehicle">drones</a>, which can launch precise missiles. They are equipped with high-resolution cameras and other sensors. In addition, the missile fired from a drone has its own cameras that allow the operator to observe the target from the moment of firing. After a missile has been launched, the drone operator can remotely divert it elsewhere. Drone operators can view objects on the ground in detail during both day and night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-precisely_wrong_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-precisely_wrong-145">[145]</a></sup> Israeli drones routinely patrol over Gaza.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buffer_Zone">Buffer Zone</span></h3>
<p>Part of the territory is depopulated because of the imposition of buffer zones on both the Israeli and Egyptian borders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_hard_times_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_hard_times-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pchr_enforced_live_fire_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-pchr_enforced_live_fire-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>Initially, Israel imposed a 50-meter buffer zone in Gaza.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imemc_2011-04-05_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-imemc_2011-04-05-149">[149]</a></sup> In 2000, it was expanded to 150 meters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pchr_enforced_live_fire_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-pchr_enforced_live_fire-147">[147]</a></sup> Following the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_Gaza" title="Israeli disengagement from Gaza">Israeli disengagement from Gaza</a>, an undefined buffer zone was maintained, including a no-fishing zone along the coast.</p>
<p>In 2009/2010, Israel expanded the buffer zone to 300 meters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha_factsheet_july_2015_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_factsheet_july_2015-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imemc_2011-04-05_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-imemc_2011-04-05-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> In 2010, the UN estimated that 30 percent of the arable land in Gaza had been lost to the buffer zone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_hard_times_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_hard_times-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imemc_2011-04-05_149-2"><a href="#cite_note-imemc_2011-04-05-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 February 2013, pursuant to a November 2012 ceasefire, Israel declared a buffer zone of 100 meters on land and 6 nautical miles offshore. In the following month, the zone was changed to 300 meters and 3 nautical miles. The 1994 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaza_Jericho_Agreement" title="Gaza Jericho Agreement">Gaza Jericho Agreement</a> allows 20 nautical miles, and the 2002 Bertini Commitment allows 12 nautical miles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha_factsheet_july_2015_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_factsheet_july_2015-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pchr_enforced_live_fire_147-2"><a href="#cite_note-pchr_enforced_live_fire-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2015, the IDF confirmed a buffer zone of 300 meters for residents and 100 meters for farmers, but without explaining how to distinguish between the two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gisha_idf_spokesman_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-gisha_idf_spokesman-151">[151]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gaza_Strip&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, on a third of Gaza's agricultural land, residents risk Israeli attacks. According to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PCHR" title="PCHR">PCHR</a>, Israeli attacks take place up to approximately 1.5 km (0.9 mi) from the border, making 17% of Gaza's total territory a risk zone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pchr_enforced_live_fire_147-3"><a href="#cite_note-pchr_enforced_live_fire-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>Israel says the buffer zone is needed to protect Israeli communities just over the border from sniper fire and rocket attacks. In the 18 months until November 2010, one Thai farm worker in Israel was killed by a rocket fired from Gaza, and in 2010, according to IDF figures, 180 rockets and mortars had been fired into Israel by militants. In 6 months, however, 11 Palestinians civilians, including four children, had been killed by Israeli fire and at least 70 Palestinian civilians were injured in the same period, including at least 49 who were working collecting rubble and scrap metal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_hard_times_146-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_hard_times-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>A buffer zone was also created on the Egyptian side of the <a href="/wiki/Gaza%E2%80%93Egypt_border#Buffer_zone" title="Gaza–Egypt border">Gaza–Egypt border</a>. In 2014, scores of homes in <a href="/wiki/Rafah,_Egypt" title="Rafah, Egypt">Rafah</a> were destroyed for the buffer zone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> According to Amnesty International, more than 800 homes had been destroyed and more than 1,000 families evicted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haaretz_abbas_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz_abbas-153">[153]</a></sup> Palestinian President Mahmoud Abbas agreed with the destruction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip_smuggling_tunnel#Measures_taken_by_Egypt" title="Gaza Strip smuggling tunnel">smuggling tunnels</a> by flooding them, and then punishing the owners of the houses that contained entrances to the tunnels, including demolishing their houses, arguing that the tunnels had produced 1,800 millionaires, and were used for smuggling weapons, drugs, cash, and equipment for forging documents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haaretz_abbas_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz_abbas-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gaza_blockade">Gaza blockade</span></h3>
<p>Israel and Egypt maintain a <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Blockade of the Gaza Strip">blockade of the Gaza Strip</a>, although Israel allows in limited quantities of medical humanitarian aid. The Red Cross claimed that the blockade harms the economy and causes a shortage of basic medicines and equipment such as painkillers and x-ray film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>Israel claims the blockade is necessary to prevent the smuggling of weapons into Gaza. For example, in 2014, a Panamanian-flagged ship claiming to be carrying construction materials was boarded by the IDF and was found to contain Syrian produced rockets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Israel maintains that the blockade is legal and necessary to limit <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel" title="Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel">Palestinian rocket attacks</a> from the Gaza Strip on its cities and to prevent Hamas from obtaining other weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaza.27s_Tunnel_Economy_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza.27s_Tunnel_Economy-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-middleeastmonitor2013_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-middleeastmonitor2013-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idf100908_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-idf100908-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>Director of the <a href="/wiki/Shin_Bet" title="Shin Bet">Shin Bet</a> (Israel Security Agency) <a href="/wiki/Yuval_Diskin" title="Yuval Diskin">Yuval Diskin</a> did not oppose easing trade restrictions, but said that <a href="/wiki/Smuggling_tunnel" title="Smuggling tunnel">smuggling tunnels</a> in Sinai and an open seaport in the Gaza Strip endangered Israel's security. According to Diskin, Hamas and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Jihad_Movement_in_Palestine" title="Islamic Jihad Movement in Palestine">Islamic Jihad</a> had smuggled in over "5,000 rockets with ranges up to 40 km (25 mi)." Some of the rockets could reach as far as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv_Metropolitan_Area" title="Tel Aviv Metropolitan Area">Tel Aviv Metropolitan Area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>Israeli spokesman Mark Regev described Israel's actions as "sanctions," not a blockade, but a Gazan legal consultant for UNRWA called the blockade "an action outside of international law.”<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2010, British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> said, "humanitarian goods and people must flow in both directions. Gaza cannot and must not be allowed to remain a prison camp."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cameron_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cameron-161">[161]</a></sup> In response, the spokesman for the <a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_Israel,_London" title="Embassy of Israel, London">Israeli embassy in London</a> said, "The people of Gaza are the prisoners of the terrorist organization Hamas. The situation in Gaza is the direct result of Hamas' rule and priorities."</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3504" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/220px-Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/330px-Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/440px-Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tent camp, April 2009, after <a href="/wiki/Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)" title="Gaza War (2008–09)">Cast Lead</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> accused Israel of waging a financial war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> The IDF strictly controlled travel within the area of the crossing points between Israel and the Gaza Strip, and sealed its border with Gaza. U.S. government travel guides warned tourists that the region was dangerous.</p>
<p>Facing mounting international pressure, Egypt and Israel lessened the restrictions starting in June 2010, when the Rafah border crossing from Egypt to Gaza was partially opened by Egypt. Egypt’s foreign ministry said that the crossing would remain open mainly for people, but not for supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Israel announced that it would allow the passage of civilian goods but not weapons and items that could be used for dual purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google1_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-google1-164">[164]</a></sup> In December 2015, Egypt asked Israel not to allow Turkish aid to get through to the Gaza Strip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> Benjamin Netanyahu said that it is impossible to lift the siege on Gaza and that the security of Israel is the primary issue for him. He confirmed "that Israel is the only country that currently sends supplies to the coastal enclave".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memo_israel_confirms_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-memo_israel_confirms-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January and February 2011, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_for_the_Coordination_of_Humanitarian_Affairs" title="United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs">United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs</a> (UNOCHA) assessed measures taken to ease the blockade<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha201103_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-ocha201103-167">[167]</a></sup> and concluded that they were helpful but not sufficient to improve the lives of the local inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha201103_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-ocha201103-167">[167]</a></sup> UNOCHA called on Israel to reduce restrictions on exports and the import of construction materials, and to lift the general ban on movement between Gaza and the West Bank via Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha201103_167-2"><a href="#cite_note-ocha201103-167">[167]</a></sup> After Egypt's President Hosni Mubarak resigned on 28 May 2011, Egypt permanently opened its border with the Gaza Strip to students, medical patients, and foreign passport holders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha201103_167-3"><a href="#cite_note-ocha201103-167">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/2013_Egyptian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2013 Egyptian coup d'état">2013 Egyptian coup d'état</a>, Egypt's military has destroyed most of the 1,200 tunnels which are used for smuggling food, weapons, and other goods to Gaza.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/August_2013_Rabaa_Massacre" title="August 2013 Rabaa Massacre">August 2013 Rabaa Massacre</a> in Egypt, the border crossing was closed 'indefinitely.'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>Israel has alternately <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goods_allowed_or_banned_for_import_into_Gaza#Import_through_Israel" title="Goods allowed or banned for import into Gaza">restricted or allowed goods</a> and people to cross the terrestrial border and handles vicariously the movement of goods into and out of Gaza by air and sea. Israel largely provides for Gaza's water supply, electricity, and communications infrastructure. While the import of food is restricted through the Gaza blockade, the Israeli military destroys agricultural crops by spraying toxic chemicals over the Gazan lands, using aircraft flying over the border zone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memo_destroying_crops_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-memo_destroying_crops-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Also Gaza's agricultural research and development station was destroyed in 2014 and again in January 2016, while import of new equipment is obstructed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Movement_of_people">Movement of people</span></h4>
<p>Because of the Israeli–Egyptian blockade, the population is not free to leave or enter the Gaza Strip. Only in exceptional cases are people allowed to pass through the <a href="/wiki/Erez_Crossing" title="Erez Crossing">Erez Crossing</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Rafah_Border_Crossing" title="Rafah Border Crossing">Rafah Border Crossing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha_factsheet_july_2015_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_factsheet_july_2015-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha_update_sept_2015_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_update_sept_2015-174">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-so_near_so_far_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-so_near_so_far-176">[176]</a></sup> In 2015, a Gazan woman was not allowed to travel through Israel to Jordan on her way to her own wedding. The Israeli authorities found she did not meet the criteria for travel, namely only in exceptional humanitarian cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>Under the long-term blockade, the Gaza Strip is often described as a "prison-camp or open air prison for its collective denizens". The comparison is done by observers, ranging from <a href="/wiki/Roger_Cohen" title="Roger Cohen">Roger Cohen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Weschler" title="Lawrence Weschler">Lawrence Weschler</a> to NGOs, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B%27tselem" title="B'tselem">B'tselem</a>, and politicians and diplomats, such as <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noam_Chomsky" title="Noam Chomsky">Noam Chomsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdoğan">Recep Tayyip Erdoğan</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Shoebridge" title="David Shoebridge">David Shoebridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Holmes_(British_diplomat)" title="John Holmes (British diplomat)">Sir John Holmes</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> In 2014 French President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francois_Hollande" title="Francois Hollande">Francois Hollande</a> called for the demilitarization of Gaza and a lifting of the blockade, saying "Gaza must neither be an open prison nor a military base."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p>An anonymous Israeli analyst has called it "Israel's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcatraz" title="Alcatraz">Alcatraz</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> While <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Booth" title="Lauren Booth">Lauren Booth</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raz2008_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raz2008-188">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shlaifer2014_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shlaifer2014-189">[189]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Philip_Slater" title="Philip Slater">Philip Slater</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slater2011_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slater2011-190">[190]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Agamben" title="Giorgio Agamben">Giorgio Agamben</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jessica2013_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jessica2013-191">[191]</a></sup> compare it to a "concentration camp". For <a href="/wiki/Robert_S._Wistrich" title="Robert S. Wistrich">Robert S. Wistrich</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> and Philip Mendes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> such analogies are designed to offend Jews, while Philip Seib dismisses the comparison as absurd, and claims that it arises from sources like Al Jazeera and statements by Arab leaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Gaza_City" title="Economy of Gaza City">Economy of Gaza City</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Palestinian_territories" title="Economy of the Palestinian territories">Economy of the Palestinian territories</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Blockade of the Gaza Strip">Blockade of the Gaza Strip</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sea_view_from_Al_Deira_hotel,_Gaza.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Sea_view_from_Al_Deira_hotel%2C_Gaza.jpg/220px-Sea_view_from_Al_Deira_hotel%2C_Gaza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Sea_view_from_Al_Deira_hotel%2C_Gaza.jpg/330px-Sea_view_from_Al_Deira_hotel%2C_Gaza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Sea_view_from_Al_Deira_hotel%2C_Gaza.jpg/440px-Sea_view_from_Al_Deira_hotel%2C_Gaza.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sea_view_from_Al_Deira_hotel,_Gaza.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sea-view from the <a href="/wiki/Al_Deira_Hotel" title="Al Deira Hotel">Al Deira Hotel</a> on the Gaza coast</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The economy of the Gaza Strip is severely hampered by Egypt and Israel's almost total blockade, the high population density, limited land access, strict internal and external security controls, the effects of Israeli military operations, and restrictions on labor and trade access across the border. <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">Per capita income</a> (PPP) was estimated at US$3,100 in 2009, a position of 164th in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-cia-195">[195]</a></sup> Seventy percent of the population is below the poverty line according to a 2009 estimate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_195-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia-195">[195]</a></sup> Gaza Strip industries are generally small family businesses that produce <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soap" title="Soap">soap</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olive-wood" title="Olive-wood">olive-wood</a> carvings, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother-of-pearl" title="Mother-of-pearl">mother-of-pearl</a> souvenirs.</p>
<p>The main agricultural products are <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">vegetables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halal" title="Halal">Halal</a> <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dairy_products" title="Dairy products">dairy products</a>. Primary exports are citrus and cut flowers, while primary imports are food, consumer goods, and construction materials. The main trade partners of the Gaza Strip are Israel and Egypt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_195-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU" title="EU">EU</a> described the Gaza economy as follows: "Since Hamas took control of Gaza in 2007 and following the closure imposed by Israel, the situation in the Strip has been one of chronic need, de-development and donor dependency, despite a temporary relaxation on restrictions in movement of people and goods after the Gaza flotilla raid in 2010. The closure has effectively cut off access for exports to traditional markets in Israel, transfers to the West Bank and has severely restricted imports. Exports are now down to 2% of 2007 levels."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eccpalestine.org_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-eccpalestine.org-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Sara Roy, one senior IDF officer told an UNWRA official in 2015 that Israel's policy towards the Gaza Strip consisted of: "No development, no prosperity, no humanitarian crisis."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p><span id="Under_Palestinian_authority_.281994-2007.29"></span></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_Oslo_.281994.E2.80.932007.29">After Oslo (1994–2007)</span></h3>
<p>Economic output in the Gaza Strip declined by about one-third between 1992 and 1996. This downturn was attributed to Israeli closure policies and, to a lesser extent, corruption and mismanagement by <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>. Economic development has been hindered by Israel refusing to allow the operation of a sea harbour. A <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Seaport_plans" title="Gaza Seaport plans">Gaza Seaport</a> was planned to be built in Gaza with help from France and The Netherlands, but the project was bombed by Israel in 2001. Israel said that the reason for bombing was that Israeli settlements were being shot at from the construction site at the harbour. As a result, international transports (both trade and aid) had to go through Israel, which was hindered by the imposition of generalized border closures. These also disrupted previously established labor and commodity market relationships between Israel and the Strip. A serious negative social effect of this downturn was the emergence of high unemployment.</p>
<p>For its energy, Gaza is largely dependent on Israel either for import of electricity or fuel for its sole power plant. The <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a> set limits for the Palestinian production and importation of energy. Pursuant to the Accords, the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Electric_Corporation" title="Israel Electric Corporation">Israel Electric Corporation</a> exclusively supplies the electricity (63% of the total consumption in 2013).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unctad-2015_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-unctad-2015-21">[21]</a></sup> The amount of electricity has consistently been limited to 120 megawatts, which is the amount Israel undertook to sell to Gaza pursuant to the Oslo Accords.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GazaTextiles.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="553" data-file-width="793" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/GazaTextiles.jpg/220px-GazaTextiles.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/GazaTextiles.jpg/330px-GazaTextiles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/GazaTextiles.jpg/440px-GazaTextiles.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GazaTextiles.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Backyard industry</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Israel's use of comprehensive closures decreased over the next few years. In 1998, Israel implemented new policies to ease security procedures and allow somewhat freer movement of Gazan goods and labor into Israel. These changes led to three years of economic recovery in the Gaza Strip, disrupted by the outbreak of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Intifada" title="Al-Aqsa Intifada">al-Aqsa Intifada</a> in the last quarter of 2000. Before the second Palestinian uprising in September 2000, around 25,000 workers from the Gaza Strip (about 2% of the population) worked in Israel on a daily basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Second_Intifada" title="Second Intifada">Second Intifada</a> led to a steep decline in the economy of Gaza, which was heavily reliant upon external markets. Israel—which had begun its occupation by helping Gazans to plant approximately 618,000 trees in 1968, and to improve seed selection—over the first 3-year period of the second intifada, destroyed 10 percent of Gazan agricultural land, and uprooted 226,000 trees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> The population became largely dependent on humanitarian assistance, primarily from UN agencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAFB_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIAFB-200">[200]</a></sup></p>
<p>The al-Aqsa Intifada triggered tight <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">IDF</a> closures of the border with Israel, as well as frequent curbs on traffic in Palestinian self-rule areas, severely disrupting trade and labor movements. In 2001, and even more so in early 2002, internal turmoil and Israeli military measures led to widespread business closures and a sharp drop in <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>. Civilian infrastructure, such as the Palestine airport, was destroyed by Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zembla.vara.nl_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-zembla.vara.nl-201">[201]</a></sup> Another major factor was a drop in income due to reduction in the number of Gazans permitted entry to work in Israel. After the Israeli withdrawal from Gaza, the flow of a limited number of workers into Israel resumed, although Israel said it would reduce or end such permits due to the victory of <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_legislative_election,_2006" title="Palestinian legislative election, 2006">2006 parliamentary elections</a>.</p>
<p>The Israeli settlers of <a href="/wiki/Gush_Katif" title="Gush Katif">Gush Katif</a> built <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse" title="Greenhouse">greenhouses</a> and experimented with new forms of agriculture. These greenhouses provided employment for hundreds of Gazans. When Israel withdrew from the Gaza Strip in the summer of 2005, more than 3,000 (about half) of the greenhouses were purchased with $14 million raised by former <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> president <a href="/wiki/James_Wolfensohn" title="James Wolfensohn">James Wolfensohn</a>, and given to Palestinians to jump-start their economy. The rest were demolished by the departing settlers before there were offered a compensation as an inducement to leave them behind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The farming effort faltered due to limited water supply, Palestinian looting, restrictions on exports, and corruption in the Palestinian Authority. Many Palestinian companies repaired the greenhouses damaged and looted by the Palestinians after the Israeli withdrawal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, after the Israeli withdrawal from the Gaza Strip, Gaza businessmen envisaged a "magnificent future". $1.1 million was invested in an upscale restaurant, Roots, and plans were made to turn one of the Israeli settlements into a family resort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Following_Hamas_takeover_.282007-present.29">Following Hamas takeover (2007-present)</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> states: "Gaza has experienced continuous economic decline since the imposition of a closure policy by Israel in 2007. This has had serious social and humanitarian consequences for many of its 1.7 million inhabitants. The situation has deteriorated further in recent months as a result of the geo-political changes which took place in the region during the course of 2013, particularly in Egypt and its closure of the majority of smuggling tunnels between Egypt and Gaza as well as increased restrictions at Rafah."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eccpalestine.org_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-eccpalestine.org-56">[56]</a></sup> Israel, the United States, Canada, and the European Union have frozen all funds to the Palestinian government after the formation of a Hamas-controlled government after its democratic victory in the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_legislative_election,_2006" title="Palestinian legislative election, 2006">2006 Palestinian legislative election</a>. They view the group as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrorist" title="Terrorist">terrorist</a> organization, and have pressured Hamas to recognize Israel, renounce violence, and make good on past agreements. Prior to disengagement, 120,000 Palestinians from Gaza had been employed in Israel or in joint projects. After the Israeli withdrawal, the gross domestic product of the Gaza Strip declined. Jewish enterprises shut down, work relationships were severed, and job opportunities in Israel dried up. After the 2006 elections, fighting broke out between Fatah and Hamas, which Hamas won in the Gaza Strip on 14 June 2007. Israel imposed a blockade, and the only goods permitted into the Strip through the land crossings were goods of a humanitarian nature, and these were permitted in limited quantities.</p>
<p>An easing of Israel's closure policy in 2010 resulted in an improvement in some economic indicators, although exports were still restricted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAFB_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIAFB-200">[200]</a></sup> According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Defense_Forces" title="Israeli Defense Forces">Israeli Defense Forces</a> and the Palestinian Central Bureau of Statistics, the economy of the Gaza Strip improved in 2011, with a drop in unemployment and an increase in GDP. New malls opened and local industry began to develop. This economic upswing has led to the construction of hotels and a rise in the import of cars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> Wide-scale development has been made possible by the unhindered movement of goods into Gaza through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kerem_Shalom_Crossing" title="Kerem Shalom Crossing">Kerem Shalom Crossing</a> and tunnels between the Gaza Strip and Egypt. The current rate of trucks entering Gaza through Kerem Shalom is 250 trucks per day. The increase in building activity has led to a shortage of construction workers. To make up for the deficit, young people are being sent to learn the trade in Turkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, Hamas leader <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Zahar" title="Mahmoud Zahar">Mahmoud Zahar</a> said that Gaza's economic situation has improved and Gaza has become self-reliant "in several aspects except petroleum and electricity" despite Israel's blockade. Zahar said that Gaza's economic conditions are better than those in the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zahar_Maan_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zahar_Maan-207">[207]</a></sup> In 2014, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU" title="EU">EU</a>'s opinion was: "Today, Gaza is facing a dangerous and pressing humanitarian and economic situation with power outages across Gaza for up to 16 hours a day and, as a consequence, the closure of sewage pumping operations, reduced access to clean water; a reduction in medical supplies and equipment; the cessation of imports of construction materials; rising unemployment, rising prices and increased food insecurity. If left unaddressed, the situation could have serious consequences for stability in Gaza, for security more widely in the region as well as for the peace process itself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eccpalestine.org_56-3"><a href="#cite_note-eccpalestine.org-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_fuel_crisis">2012 fuel crisis</span></h4>
<p>Usually, diesel for Gaza came from Israel,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> but in 2011, Hamas started to buy cheaper fuel from Egypt, bringing it via a network of underground tunnels, and refused to allow it from Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomberg.com_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg.com-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early 2012, due to internal economic disagreement between the Palestinian Authority and the Hamas Government in Gaza, decreased supplies from Egypt and through tunnel smuggling, and Hamas's refusal to ship fuel via Israel, the Gaza Strip plunged into a fuel crisis, bringing increasingly long electricity shut downs and disruption of transportation. Egypt had attempted for a while to stop the use of underground tunnels for delivery of Egyptian fuel purchased by Palestinian authorities, and had severely reduced supply through the tunnel network. As the crisis broke out, Hamas sought to equip the Rafah terminal between Egypt and Gaza for fuel transfer, and refused to accept fuel to be delivered via the Kerem Shalom crossing between Israel and Gaza.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<p>In mid-February 2012, as the crisis escalated, Hamas rejected an <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egyptian</a> proposal to bring in fuel via the Kerem Shalom Crossing between Israel and Gaza to reactivate Gaza's only power plant. Ahmed Abu Al-Amreen of the Hamas-run Energy Authority refused it on the grounds that the crossing is operated by Israel and Hamas' fierce opposition to the existence of Israel. Egypt cannot ship <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">diesel fuel</a> to Gaza directly through the Rafah crossing point, because it is limited to the movement of individuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomberg.com_209-1"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg.com-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early March 2012, the head of Gaza's energy authority stated that Egypt wanted to transfer energy via the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kerem_Shalom_Crossing" title="Kerem Shalom Crossing">Kerem Shalom Crossing</a>, but he personally refused it to go through the "Zionist entity" (Israel) and insisted that Egypt transfer the fuel through the Rafah Crossing, although this crossing is not equipped to handle the half-million liters needed each day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late March 2012, Hamas began offering carpools for people to use Hamas state vehicles to get to work. Many Gazans began to wonder how these vehicles have fuel themselves, as diesel was completely unavailable in Gaza, ambulances could no longer be used, but Hamas government officials still had fuel for their own cars. Many Gazans said that Hamas confiscated the fuel it needed from petrol stations and used it exclusively for their own purposes.</p>
<p>Egypt agreed to provide 600,000 liters of fuel to Gaza daily, but it had no way of delivering it that Hamas would agree to.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition, Israel introduced a number of goods and vehicles into the Gaza Strip via the Kerem Shalom Crossing, as well as the normal diesel for hospitals. Israel also shipped 150,000 liters of diesel through the crossing, which was paid for by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a>.</p>
<p>In April 2012, the issue was resolved as certain amounts of fuel were supplied with the involvement of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a>, after the Palestinian Authority and Hamas reached a deal. Fuel was finally transferred via the Israeli Kerem Shalom Crossing, which Hamas previously refused to transfer fuel from.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_budget">Current budget</span></h4>
<p>Most of the Gaza Strip administration funding comes from outside as an aid, with large portion delivered by UN organizations directly to education and food supply. Most of the Gaza GDP comes as foreign humanitarian and direct economic support. Of those funds, the major part is supported by the U.S. and the European Union. Portions of the direct economic support have been provided by the Arab League, though it largely has not provided funds according to schedule. Among other alleged sources of Gaza administration budget is Iran.</p>
<p>A diplomatic source told Reuters that Iran had funded Hamas in the past with up to $300 million per year, but the flow of money had not been regular in 2011. "Payment has been in suspension since August," said the source.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alarabiya3001_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-alarabiya3001-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 2012, some diplomatic sources said that Turkey promised to provide Haniyeh's Gaza Strip administration with $300 million to support its annual budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alarabiya3001_214-1"><a href="#cite_note-alarabiya3001-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 2012, the Hamas government in Gaza approved its budget for 2012, which was up 25 percent year-on-year over 2011 budget, indicating that donors, including Iran, benefactors in the Islamic world, and Palestinian expatriates, are still heavily funding the movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa0204_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-aa0204-215">[215]</a></sup> Chief of Gaza's parliament's budget committee Jamal Nassar said the 2012 budget is $769 million, compared to $630 million in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa0204_215-1"><a href="#cite_note-aa0204-215">[215]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span></h2>
<p><span id="Geography"></span> The Gaza Strip is located in the Middle East (at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Gaza_Strip&amp;params=31_25_N_34_20_E_region:PS_type:adm1st_scale:300000"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">31°25′N</span> <span class="longitude">34°20′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">31.417°N 34.333°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">31.417; 34.333</span></span></span></a></span><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Gaza_Strip&amp;params=31_25_N_34_20_E_region:PS_type:adm1st_scale:300000"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">31°25′N</span> <span class="longitude">34°20′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">31.417°N 34.333°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">31.417; 34.333</span></span></span></a></span></span></span>). It has a 51 kilometers (32 mi) border with <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, and an 11 km (7 mi) border with <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, near the city of <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a>. <a href="/wiki/Khan_Yunis" title="Khan Yunis">Khan Yunis</a> is located 7 kilometers (4.3 mi) northeast of Rafah, and several towns around <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deir_el-Balah" title="Deir el-Balah">Deir el-Balah</a> are located along the coast between it and <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza City</a>. <a href="/wiki/Beit_Lahia" title="Beit Lahia">Beit Lahia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beit_Hanoun" title="Beit Hanoun">Beit Hanoun</a> are located to the north and northeast of Gaza City, respectively. The <a href="/wiki/Gush_Katif" title="Gush Katif">Gush Katif</a> bloc of Israeli settlements used to exist on the <a href="/wiki/Dune" title="Dune">sand dunes</a> adjacent to Rafah and Khan Yunis, along the southwestern edge of the 40 kilometers (25 mi) <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> coastline. Al Deira beach is a popular venue for surfers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Gaza Strip has an arid climate, with mild winters, and dry, hot summers subject to <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">drought</a>. The terrain is flat or rolling, with dunes near the coast. The highest point is Abu 'Awdah (Joz Abu 'Auda), at 105 meters (344 ft) above <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>. Environmental problems include <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>; <a href="/wiki/Biosalinity" title="Biosalinity">salination</a> of fresh water; <a href="/wiki/Sewage_treatment" title="Sewage treatment">sewage treatment</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water-borne_disease" title="Water-borne disease">water-borne diseases</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soil_degradation" title="Soil degradation">soil degradation</a>; and depletion and contamination of underground water resources.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</span></h2>
<p>Natural resources of Gaza include <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a>—about a third of the strip is irrigated. Recently, <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> was discovered. Environmental problems include <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>; <a href="/wiki/Biosalinity" title="Biosalinity">salination</a> of fresh water; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water-borne_disease" title="Water-borne disease">water-borne disease</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soil_degradation" title="Soil degradation">soil degradation</a>; lack of adequate <a href="/wiki/Sewage_treatment" title="Sewage treatment">sewage treatment</a>; and depletion and contamination of underground water resources. The Gaza Strip is largely dependent on water from <a href="/wiki/HaBesor_Stream" title="HaBesor Stream">Wadi Gaza</a>, which also supplies Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google2_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-google2-217">[217]</a></sup></p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_in_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Natural gas in the Gaza Strip">Natural gas in the Gaza Strip</a></div>
<p>Gaza's marine gas reserves extend 32 kilometres from the Gaza Strip's coastline<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nafeez_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nafeez-218">[218]</a></sup> and were calculated at 35 BCM.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rand_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rand-219">[219]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Palestinian_territories" title="Demographics of the Palestinian territories">Demographics of the Palestinian territories</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Girls_lining_up_for_class_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Girls_lining_up_for_class_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/220px-Girls_lining_up_for_class_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Girls_lining_up_for_class_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/330px-Girls_lining_up_for_class_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Girls_lining_up_for_class_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/440px-Girls_lining_up_for_class_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Girls_lining_up_for_class_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Schoolgirls in Gaza lining up for class, 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2010 approximately 1.6 million Palestinians lived in the Gaza Strip,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_195-3"><a href="#cite_note-cia-195">[195]</a></sup> almost 1.0 million of them UN-registered refugees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> The majority of the Palestinians descend from refugees who were driven from or left their homes during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1948_Arab-Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab-Israeli War">1948 Arab-Israeli War</a>. The Strip's population has continued to increase since that time, one of the main reasons being a <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of 4.24 children per woman (2014 est). In a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_fertility_rate" title="List of countries by fertility rate">ranking by total fertility rate</a>, this places Gaza 34th of 224 regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_195-4"><a href="#cite_note-cia-195">[195]</a></sup> According to the UN, unless remedial steps are taken to repair the basic infrastructure by 2020, with a further demographic increase of 500,000 and intensified housing problems, the Gaza Strip will become effectively uninhabitable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslim" title="Sunni Muslim">Sunni Muslims</a> make up the predominant part of the Palestinian population in the Gaza Strip.</p>
<p>Most of the inhabitants are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslims" title="Sunni Muslims">Sunni Muslims</a>, with an estimated 2,000 to 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Arab_Christians" title="Arab Christians">Arab Christians</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> making the region 99.8 percent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslim" title="Sunni Muslim">Sunni Muslim</a> and 0.2 percent Christian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_195-5"><a href="#cite_note-cia-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion_and_culture">Religion and culture</span></h2>
