<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_compliance_of_population_to_Islam">Religious compliance of population to Islam</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamization_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Islamization of the Gaza Strip">Islamization of the Gaza Strip</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_law_in_Gaza">Islamic law in Gaza</span></h4>
<p>From 1987 to 1991, during the <a href="/wiki/First_Intifada" title="First Intifada">First Intifada</a>, Hamas campaigned for the wearing of the <a href="/wiki/Hijab" title="Hijab">hijab</a> head-cover and for other measures (such as the promotion of <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamy</a>, segregating women from men and insisting they stay at home).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the course of this campaign, women who chose not to wear the hijab were verbally and physically harassed by Hamas activists, leading to hijabs being worn "just to avoid problems on the streets".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruben_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ruben-224">[224]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2000, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_extremist" title="Islamic extremist">Islamic extremists</a> burned down the Windmill Hotel, owned by Basil Eleiwa, when they learned it had served alcohol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since Hamas took over in 2007, attempts have been made by Islamist activists to impose "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_dress" title="Islamic dress">Islamic dress</a>" and to require women to wear the hijab.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-226">[226]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xinhua_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua-227">[227]</a></sup> The government's "Islamic Endowment Ministry" has deployed <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Virtue_Committee&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Virtue Committee (page does not exist)">Virtue Committee</a> members to warn citizens of the dangers of immodest dress, card playing and dating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomberg_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-228">[228]</a></sup> However, there are no government laws imposing dress and other moral standards, and the Hamas education ministry reversed one effort to impose Islamic dress on students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_226-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-226">[226]</a></sup> There has also been successful resistance<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (May 2015)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to attempts by local Hamas officials to impose Islamic dress on women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, the Hamas-controlled government stepped up its efforts to "Islamize" Gaza in 2010, efforts it says included the "repression of civil society" and "severe violations of personal freedom."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Esveld_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-Esveld-230">[230]</a></sup></p>
<p>Palestinian researcher Khaled Al-Hroub has criticized what he called the "<a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a>-like steps" Hamas has taken: "The Islamization that has been forced upon the Gaza Strip—the suppression of social, cultural, and press freedoms that do not suit Hamas's view[s]—is an egregious deed that must be opposed. It is the reenactment, under a religious guise, of the experience of [other] totalitarian regimes and dictatorships."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> Hamas officials denied having any plans to impose Islamic law. One legislator stated that "[w]hat you are seeing are incidents, not policy" and that "we believe in persuasion".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomberg_228-1"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-228">[228]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2012 Gaza youth complained that security officers had obstructed their freedom to wear saggy pants and to have haircuts of their own choosing, and that they faced being arrested. Youth in Gaza are also arrested by security officers for wearing shorts and for showing their legs, which have been described by youth as embarrassing incidents, and one youth explained that "My saggy pants did not harm anyone." However, a spokesman for Gaza's Ministry of Interior denied such a campaign, and denied interfering in the lives of Gaza citizens, but explained that "maintaining the morals and values of the Palestinian society is highly required".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_politics">Islamic politics</span></h4>
<p>Iran was the largest state supporter of Hamas, and the Muslim Brotherhood also gave support, but these political relationships have recently been disrupted following the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a> by Iranian support for and the position of Hamas has declined as support diminishes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eccpalestine.org_56-4"><a href="#cite_note-eccpalestine.org-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Salafism">Salafism</span></h4>
<p>In addition to Hamas, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salafist" title="Salafist">Salafist</a> movement began to appear about 2005 in Gaza, characterized by "a strict lifestyle based on that of the earliest followers of Islam".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-salafist_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-salafist-233">[233]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gaza_Strip&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there are estimated to be only "hundreds or perhaps a few thousand" Salafists in Gaza.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-salafist_233-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-salafist-233">[233]</a></sup> However, the failure of Hamas to lift the Israeli blockade of Gaza despite thousands of casualties and much destruction during <a href="/wiki/Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)" title="Gaza War (2008–09)">2008-9</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="2014 Israel–Gaza conflict">2014 wars</a> has weakened Hamas's support and led some in Hamas to be concerned about the possibility of defections to the Salafist "<a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-salafist_233-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-salafist-233">[233]</a></sup></p>
<p>The movement has clashed with Hamas on a number of occasions. In 2009, a Salafist leader, Abdul Latif Moussa, declared an Islamic emirate in the town of Rafah, on Gaza's southern border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-salafist_233-3"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-salafist-233">[233]</a></sup> Moussa and 19 other people were killed when Hamas forces stormed his mosque and house. In 2011, Salafists abducted and murdered a pro-Palestinian Italian activist, Vittorio Arrigoni. Following this Hamas again took action to crush the Salafist groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-salafist_233-4"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-salafist-233">[233]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Archaeology">Archaeology</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Museum_of_Archaeology" title="Gaza Museum of Archaeology">Gaza Museum of Archaeology</a> was established by Jawdat N. Khoudary in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes08_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes08-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ucas1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Ucas1.jpg/220px-Ucas1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Ucas1.jpg/330px-Ucas1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Ucas1.jpg/440px-Ucas1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ucas1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/University_College_of_Applied_Sciences" title="University College of Applied Sciences">University College of Applied Sciences</a>, the largest college in Gaza</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2010, illiteracy among Gazan youth was less than 1%. In 2012, there were five universities in the Gaza Strip and eight new schools are under construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> According to UNRWA figures, there are 640 schools in Gaza: 383 government schools, 221 <a href="/wiki/UNRWA" title="UNRWA">UNRWA</a> schools and 36 private schools, serving a total of 441,452 students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, Al Zahara, a private school in central Gaza introduced a special program for mental development based on math computations. The program was created in Malaysia in 1993, according to the school principal, Majed al-Bari.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Community College of Applied Science and Technology (CCAST) was established in 1998 in Gaza City. In 2003, the college moved into its new campus and established the Gaza Polytechnic Institute (GPI) in 2006 in southern Gaza. In 2007, the college received accreditation to award BA degrees as the <a href="/wiki/University_College_of_Applied_Sciences" title="University College of Applied Sciences">University College of Applied Sciences</a> (UCAS). In 2010, the college had a student population of 6,000 in eight departments offering over 40 majors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2011, some Gazans, upset that UNRWA did not rebuild their homes that were lost in the Second Intifada, blocked UNRWA from performing its services and shut down UNRWA's summer camps. Gaza residents also closed UNRWA's emergency department, social services office and ration stores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mosque_conf_hall_iug.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="436" data-file-width="640" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8c/Mosque_conf_hall_iug.jpg/220px-Mosque_conf_hall_iug.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8c/Mosque_conf_hall_iug.jpg/330px-Mosque_conf_hall_iug.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8c/Mosque_conf_hall_iug.jpg/440px-Mosque_conf_hall_iug.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mosque_conf_hall_iug.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Islamic_University_of_Gaza" title="Islamic University of Gaza">Islamic University of Gaza</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span></h3>
<p>In Gaza, there are hospitals and additional healthcare facilities. Because of the high number of young people the <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">mortality rate</a> is one of the lowest in the world, at 0.315% per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> The infant mortality rate is ranked 105th highest out of 224 countries and territories, at 16.55 deaths per 1,000 births.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> The Gaza Strip places 24th out of 135 countries according to <a href="/wiki/Human_Poverty_Index" title="Human Poverty Index">Human Poverty Index</a>.</p>
<p>A study carried out by <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University</a> (U.S.) and <a href="/wiki/Al-Quds_University" title="Al-Quds University">Al-Quds University</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dis" title="Abu Dis">Abu Dis</a>) for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cooperative_for_Assistance_and_Relief_Everywhere" title="Cooperative for Assistance and Relief Everywhere">CARE International</a> in late 2002 revealed very high levels of dietary deficiency among the Palestinian population. The study found that 17.5% of children aged 6–59 months suffered from chronic <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a>. 53% of women of reproductive age and 44% of children were found to be <a href="/wiki/Anemia" title="Anemia">anemic</a>. Insecurity in obtaining sufficient food as of 2016 affects roughly 70% of Gaza households, as the number of people requiring assistance from UN agencies has risen from 72,000 in 2000, to 800,000 in 2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the Hamas takeover of the Gaza Strip health conditions in Gaza Strip faced new challenges. <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) expressed its concerns about the consequences of the Palestinian internal political fragmentation; the socioeconomic decline; military actions; and the physical, psychological and economic isolation on the health of the population in Gaza.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> In a 2012 study of the occupied territories, the WHO reported that roughly 50% of the young children and infants under two years old and 39.1% of pregnant women receiving antenatal services care in Gaza suffer from iron-deficiency anemia. The organization also observed chronic malnutrition in children under five "is not improving and may be deteriorating."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup></p>
<p>Dr. Mohammed Abu Shaban, director of the Blood Tumors Department in Al-Rantisy Hospital in Gaza witnessed an increase in blood cancer. In March 2010 the department had seen 55 cases that year, compared to 20 to 25 cases normally seen in an entire year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (June 2010)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata">– <a href="/wiki/Talk:Gaza_Strip#Dubious" title="Talk:Gaza Strip">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a>, the average life expectancy in the Gaza Strip is 72.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare_availability">Healthcare availability</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Khalida_Jarrar#Israeli_denial_of_medical_treatment" title="Khalida Jarrar">Khalida Jarrar § Israeli denial of medical treatment</a></div>
<p>According to Palestinian leaders in the Gaza Strip, the majority of medical aid delivered are "past their expiration date." Mounir el-Barash, the director of donations in Gaza's health department, claims 30% of aid sent to Gaza is used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gazans who desire medical care in Israeli hospitals must apply for a medical visa permit. In 2007, State of Israel granted 7,176 permits and denied 1,627.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, two hospitals funded by Turkey and Saudi Arabia were under construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_sports">Culture and sports</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D9%85%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86%D8%A9_%D8%A3%D8%B5%D8%AF%D8%A7%D8%A1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/%D9%85%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86%D8%A9_%D8%A3%D8%B5%D8%AF%D8%A7%D8%A1.jpg/220px-%D9%85%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86%D8%A9_%D8%A3%D8%B5%D8%AF%D8%A7%D8%A1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/%D9%85%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86%D8%A9_%D8%A3%D8%B5%D8%AF%D8%A7%D8%A1.jpg/330px-%D9%85%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86%D8%A9_%D8%A3%D8%B5%D8%AF%D8%A7%D8%A1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/%D9%85%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86%D8%A9_%D8%A3%D8%B5%D8%AF%D8%A7%D8%A1.jpg/440px-%D9%85%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86%D8%A9_%D8%A3%D8%B5%D8%AF%D8%A7%D8%A1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_arts">Fine arts</span></h3>
<p>The Gaza Strip has been home to a significant branch of the contemporary Palestinian art movement since the mid 20th century. Notable artists include painters Ismail Ashour, Shafiq Redwan, Bashir Senwar, Majed Shalla, Fayez Sersawi, Abdul Rahman al Muzayan and Ismail Shammout, and media artists Taysir Batniji (who lives in France) and <a href="/wiki/Laila_Shawa" title="Laila Shawa">Laila al Shawa</a> (who lives in London). An emerging generation of artists is also active in nonprofit art organizations such as Windows From Gaza and Eltiqa Group, which regularly host exhibitions and events open to the public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span></h3>
<p>In 2010, Gaza inaugurated its first <a href="/wiki/Olympic-size_swimming_pool" title="Olympic-size swimming pool">Olympic-size swimming pool</a> at the <a href="/wiki/As-Sadaka" title="As-Sadaka">As-Sadaka</a> club. The opening ceremony was held by the Islamic Society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maan_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-Maan-253">[253]</a></sup> The swimming team of as-Sadaka holds several gold and silver medals from Palestinian swimming competitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadaka_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-sadaka-254">[254]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_and_communications">Transport and communications</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gaza_airport_03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="700" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Gaza_airport_03.jpg/220px-Gaza_airport_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Gaza_airport_03.jpg/330px-Gaza_airport_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Gaza_airport_03.jpg/440px-Gaza_airport_03.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gaza_airport_03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damaged part of Gaza airport, May 2002</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a> ceded control of the <a href="/wiki/Airspace" title="Airspace">airspace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Territorial_waters" title="Territorial waters">territorial waters</a> to Israel. Any external travel from Gaza requires cooperation from either Egypt or Israel.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Highways">Highways</span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Salah_al-Din_Road" title="Salah al-Din Road">Salah al-Din Road</a> (also known as the Salah ad-Deen Highway) is the main highway of the Gaza Strip and extends over 45 km (28 mi), spanning the entire length of the territory from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rafah_Crossing" title="Rafah Crossing">Rafah Crossing</a> in the south to the <a href="/wiki/Erez_Crossing" title="Erez Crossing">Erez Crossing</a> in the north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-National_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-National-255">[255]</a></sup> The road is named after the 12th-century <a href="/wiki/Ayyubid_dynasty" title="Ayyubid dynasty">Ayyubid</a> general <a href="/wiki/Saladin" title="Saladin">Salah al-Din</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_transport">Rail transport</span></h4>
<p>Former railway: see <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Railways#Railway_in_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Palestine Railways">Palestine Railways#Railway in the Gaza Strip</a></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_transport">Marine transport</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Gaza" title="Port of Gaza">Port of Gaza</a> has been an important and active port since antiquity. Despite <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaza_Seaport_Plans" title="Gaza Seaport Plans">plans</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_I_Accord" title="Oslo I Accord">Oslo Peace Accords</a> to expand the port, it has been under a <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Blockade of the Gaza Strip">blockade</a> since Hamas was elected as a majority party in the 2006 elections. Both <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip#Naval_Blockade" title="Blockade of the Gaza Strip">the Israeli Navy</a> and Egypt enforce the blockade, which continues currently and has limited many aspects of life in Gaza, especially, according to Human Rights Watch, the movement of people and commerce, with exports being most affected. The improvement and rebuilding of infrastructure is also negatively impacted by these sanctions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> Plans to expand the port were halted after the outbreak of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Intifada" title="Al-Aqsa Intifada">al-Aqsa Intifada</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">Air transport</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat_International_Airport" title="Yasser Arafat International Airport">Yasser Arafat International Airport</a> opened on 24 November 1998 after the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_II_Accord" title="Oslo II Accord">Oslo II Accord</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Wye_River_Memorandum" title="Wye River Memorandum">Wye River Memorandum</a>. It was closed by Israel in October 2000. Its radar station and control tower were destroyed by Israel Defense Forces aircraft in 2001 during the al-Aqsa Intifada, and bulldozers razed the runway in January 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc_fly_again_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc_fly_again-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc2005_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2005-144">[144]</a></sup> The only remaining runway in the strip, at the <a href="/wiki/Gush_Katif_Airport" title="Gush Katif Airport">Gush Katif Airport</a>, fell into disuse following Israeli disengagement. The airspace over Gaza may be restricted by the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force" title="Israeli Air Force">Israeli Air Force</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a> authorized.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Telephone_service">Telephone service</span></h4>
<p>The Gaza Strip has rudimentary land line telephone service provided by an open-wire system, as well as extensive mobile telephone services provided by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=PalTel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="PalTel (page does not exist)">PalTel</a> (Jawwal) and Israeli providers such as <a href="/wiki/Cellcom_(Israel)" title="Cellcom (Israel)">Cellcom</a>. Gaza is serviced by four <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">internet service providers</a> that now compete for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ADSL" title="ADSL">ADSL</a> and dial-up customers.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_and_radio">Television and radio</span></h4>
<p>Most Gaza households have a radio and a TV (70%+), and approximately 20% have a <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computer</a>. People living in Gaza have access to <a href="/wiki/Free-to-air" title="Free-to-air">FTA</a> satellite programs, broadcast TV from the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Palestinian Broadcasting Corporation">Palestinian Broadcasting Corporation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Broadcasting_Authority" title="Israel Broadcasting Authority">Israel Broadcasting Authority</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Israeli_Broadcasting_Authority" title="Second Israeli Broadcasting Authority">Second Israeli Broadcasting Authority</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Joshua Castellino, Kathleen A. <li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Tristan Dunning, <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=4jp-CwAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA212" rel="nofollow"><i>Hamas, Jihad and Popular Legitimacy: Reinterpreting Resistance in Palestine,</i></a> Routledge, 2016 p.212:'Since taking sole control of Gaza in June 2007, Hamas has proven itself to be a remarkably resilient and resourceful government entity. The movement has clearly entrenched itself as the hegemonic power in the coastal enclave to such an extent that the International Crisis Group contends that the power struggle in Gaza is no longer between Hamas and Fatah. Rather the main source of confrontation is between Hamas and other more hardline Islamists and <i>salafists</i>. . . Hamas has been far more successful in an administrative sense than the Palestinian Authority in the West Bank, despite having access to only a fraction of the resources.'</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Sara_Roy" title="Sara Roy">Sara Roy</a>, <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=mX1dAAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA41" rel="nofollow"><i>Hamas and Civil Society in Gaza: Engaging the Islamist Social Sector,</i></a> Princeton University Press, 2013 p.41:'Hamas's democratic victory, however, was short-lived . .followed as it was in June 2006 by an Israeli and U.S.-led international political and economic boycott of the new Palestinian government. The boycott amounted to a form of collective punishment against the entire Palestinian population and, to my knowledge, was the first time in the history of the conflict that the international community imposed sanctions on the occupied rather than the occupier.'</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Palestinians: In Search of a Just Peace - Page 52, Cheryl Rubenberg - 2003</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-unctad-2015-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-unctad-2015_21-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-unctad-2015_21-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://unctad.org/en/PublicationsLibrary/tdb62d3_en.pdf" rel="nofollow"><i>Report on UNCTAD assistance to the Palestinian people: Developments in the economy of the Occupied Palestinian Territory</i></a>, para 20. TD/B/62/3). <a class="external text" href="http://unctad.org/en/Pages/PressRelease.aspx?OriginalVersionID=260" rel="nofollow">Source</a>.<br/>
para 40: "The study stressed that Gaza's population would increase from 1.6 million in 2011 to 2.1 million in 2020, and concluded that for Gaza to be a liveable place in 2020 "herculean efforts" needed to be accelerated in such sectors as health, education, energy, water and sanitation (United Nations, 2012). However, instead of such efforts, the tragedy in Gaza has deteriorated and its de-development was accelerated by destruction in 2014." para 43: "The social, health and security-related ramifications of the high population density and overcrowding are among the factors that may render Gaza unliveable by 2020, if present trends continue"</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-occ-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-occ_22-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-occ_22-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-occ_22-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-occ_22-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Sanger, Andrew (2011). M.N. Schmitt, Louise Arimatsu, Tim McCormack, eds. <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=hYiIWVlpFzEC&amp;pg=PA429#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">"The Contemporary Law of Blockade and the Gaza Freedom Flotilla"</a>. <i>Yearbook of International Humanitarian Law 2010</i>. Springer Science &amp; Business Media. <b>13</b>: 429. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1007%2F978-90-6704-811-8_14" rel="nofollow">10.1007/978-90-6704-811-8_14</a>. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9789067048118" title="Special:BookSources/9789067048118">9789067048118</a>. <q>Israel claims it no longer occupies the Gaza Strip, maintaining that it is neither a Stale nor a territory occupied or controlled by Israel, but rather it has 'sui generis' status. Pursuant to the Disengagement Plan, Israel dismantled all military institutions and settlements in Gaza and there is no longer a permanent Israeli military or civilian presence in the territory. However the Plan also provided that Israel will guard and monitor the external land perimeter of the Gaza Strip, will continue to maintain exclusive authority in Gaza air space, and will continue to exercise security activity in the sea off the coast of the Gaza Strip as well as maintaining an Israeli military presence on the Egyptian-Gaza border. and reserving the right to reenter Gaza at will.<br/>
Israel continues to control six of Gaza's seven land crossings, its maritime borders and airspace and the movement of goods and persons in and out of the territory. Egypt controls one of Gaza's land crossings. Troops from the Israeli Defence Force regularly enter pans of the territory and/or deploy missile attacks, drones and sonic bombs into Gaza. Israel has declared a no-go buffer zone that stretches deep into Gaza: if Gazans enter this zone they are shot on sight. Gaza is also dependent on Israel for water, electricity, telecommunications and other utilities, currency, issuing IDs, and permits to enter and leave the territory. Israel also has sole control of the Palestinian Population Registry through which the Israeli Army regulates who is classified as a Palestinian and who is a Gazan or West Banker. Since 2000 aside from a limited number of exceptions Israel has refused to add people to the Palestinian Population Registry.<br/>
It is this direct external control over Gaza and indirect control over life within Gaza that has led the United Nations, the UN General Assembly, the UN Fact Finding Mission to Gaza, International human rights organisations, US Government websites, the UK Foreign and Commonwealth Office and a significant number of legal commentators, to reject the argument that Gaza is no longer occupied.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGaza+Strip&amp;rft.atitle=The+Contemporary+Law+of+Blockade+and+the+Gaza+Freedom+Flotilla&amp;rft.aufirst=Andrew&amp;rft.aulast=Sanger&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DhYiIWVlpFzEC%26pg%3DPA429%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1007%2F978-90-6704-811-8_14&amp;rft.isbn=9789067048118&amp;rft.jtitle=Yearbook+of+International+Humanitarian+Law+2010&amp;rft.pages=429&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=13"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span> <span class="citation-comment" style="display:none; color:#33aa33">CS1 maint: Uses editors parameter (<a href="/wiki/Category:CS1_maint:_Uses_editors_parameter" title="Category:CS1 maint: Uses editors parameter">link</a>)</span><br/>
* <cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Iain_Scobbie" title="Iain Scobbie">Scobbie, Iain</a> (2012). Elizabeth Wilmshurst, ed. <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=GM90Xp03uuEC&amp;pg=PA295#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow"><i>International Law and the Classification of Conflicts</i></a>. Oxford University Press. p. 295. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780199657759" title="Special:BookSources/9780199657759">9780199657759</a>. <q>Even after the accession to power of Hamas, Israel's claim that it no longer occupies Gaza has not been accepted by UN bodies, most States, nor the majority of academic commentators because of its exclusive control of its border with Gaza and crossing points including the effective control it exerted over the Rafah crossing until at least May 2011, its control of Gaza's maritime zones and airspace which constitute what Aronson terms the 'security envelope' around Gaza, as well as its ability to intervene forcibly at will in Gaza.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGaza+Strip&amp;rft.aufirst=Iain&amp;rft.aulast=Scobbie&amp;rft.btitle=International+Law+and+the+Classification+of+Conflicts&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DGM90Xp03uuEC%26pg%3DPA295%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft.isbn=9780199657759&amp;rft.pages=295&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span><br/>
* <cite class="citation book">Gawerc, Michelle (2012). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Hka8FZ4UdWUC&amp;pg=PA44#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow"><i>Prefiguring Peace: Israeli-Palestinian Peacebuilding Partnerships</i></a>. Lexington Books. p. 44. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780739166109" title="Special:BookSources/9780739166109">9780739166109</a>. <q>While Israel withdrew from the immediate territory, it remained in control of all access to and from Gaza through the border crossings, as well as through the coastline and the airspace. In addition, Gaza was dependent upon Israel for water, electricity sewage communication networks and for its trade (Gisha 2007. Dowty 2008). ln other words, while Israel maintained that its occupation of Gaza ended with its unilateral disengagement Palestinians - as well as many human right organizations and international bodies - argued that Gaza was by all intents and purposes still occupied.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGaza+Strip&amp;rft.aufirst=Michelle&amp;rft.aulast=Gawerc&amp;rft.btitle=Prefiguring+Peace%3A+Israeli-Palestinian+Peacebuilding+Partnerships&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DHka8FZ4UdWUC%26pg%3DPA44%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft.isbn=9780739166109&amp;rft.pages=44&amp;rft.pub=Lexington+Books&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Deeb-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Deeb_23-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Deeb_23-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Dennis J. Deeb II, <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=-aqJAAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA45" rel="nofollow"><i>Israel, Palestine, &amp; the Quest for Middle East Peace,</i></a> University Press of America, 2013.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/David_Rose_(journalist)" title="David Rose (journalist)">David Rose</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.vanityfair.com/news/2008/04/gaza200804" rel="nofollow">'The Gaza Bombshell,'</a> <a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a> April,2008.'The plan was for forces led by Dahlan, and armed with new weapons supplied at America’s behest, to give Fatah the muscle it needed to remove the democratically elected Hamas-led government from power. . But the secret plan backfired, resulting in a further setback for American foreign policy under Bush. Instead of driving its enemies out of power, the U.S.-backed Fatah fighters inadvertently provoked Hamas to seize total control of Gaza.'</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Sara_Roy" title="Sara Roy">Sara Roy</a>, <i>Hamas and Civil Society in Gaza,</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=mX1dAAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA45" rel="nofollow">p.45</a>.' Dahlan, who was supported by U.S. officials, has been a bitter enemy of Hamas since his 1996 crackdown on the movement. He consistently refused to accept the Palestinian unity government brokered by the Saudi government in the Mecca Agreement "and made his opposition intolerable to Hamas when he refused to subject the security forces under his command, armed and trained by the U.S., to the legitimate Palestinian unity government as agreed between Hamas and Fatah." Alistair Crooke, a former Middle East adviser to the EU foreign policy chief Javier Solana, similarly observed, "Dahlan refused to deal with (the independent interior minister appointed to the unity government), and put his troops on the streets in defiance of the interior minister. Hamas felt that they had little option but to take control of security away from forces which were in fact creating insecurity." Hence, Hamas was not attempting a coup against the government or the Fatah organization as a whole but also against Dahlan's U.S.-funded militia (and individual Fatah loyalists it blamed for the murder of Hamas members).'</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-middleeastmonitor2013-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-middleeastmonitor2013_29-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-middleeastmonitor2013_29-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Samira Shackle (14 October 2013). <a class="external text" href="https://www.middleeastmonitor.com/blogs/lifestyle/7813-israel-tightens-its-blockade-of-gaza-for-security-reasons" rel="nofollow">"Israel tightens its blockade of Gaza for 'security reasons<span style="padding-right:0.2em;">'</span>"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Monitor" title="Middle East Monitor">Middle East Monitor</a></i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGaza+Strip&amp;rft.atitle=Israel+tightens+its+blockade+of+Gaza+for+%27security+reasons%27&amp;rft.au=Samira+Shackle&amp;rft.date=2013-10-14&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.middleeastmonitor.com%2Fblogs%2Flifestyle%2F7813-israel-tightens-its-blockade-of-gaza-for-security-reasons&amp;rft.jtitle=Middle+East+Monitor&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span>:'Yet critics point out that it is not just military supplies that cannot enter Gaza, but basic construction materials, medical supplies, and food stuffs. The issue came to international attention in 2010, when a flotilla of activists attempted to break the blockade and carry humanitarian aid into Gaza. Nine were killed when the Israeli navy entered the flotilla. The incident shone a spotlight onto the blockade of Gaza. At one stage, prohibited materials included coriander, ginger, nutmeg and newspapers. A relaxation of the rules in June 2009 meant that processed hummus was allowed in, but not hummus with extras such as pine nuts or mushrooms. One of the biggest issues has been building materials. The strict restrictions on goods going into Gaza meant that it was impossible to start reconstruction work after intensive air strikes on the city in December 2008. A leaked UN report in 2009 warned that the blockade was "devastating livelihoods" and causing gradual "de-development". It pointed out that glass was prohibited; it was therefore impossible to repair shattered windows to keep out the winter rain.'</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Dion Nissenbaum. <a class="external text" href="http://washingtonbureau.typepad.com/jerusalem/2008/12/olmert-aide-supports-free-gaza.html" rel="nofollow">"Olmert aide supports free Gaza"</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McClatchy_Newspapers" title="McClatchy Newspapers">McClatchy Newspapers</a>. 8 December 2008:'Since Hamas took control of Gaza last year, Israel has dramatically reduced the amount of food, fuel and supplies going through its border crossings with Gaza that are the main Palestinian lifeline to the outside world. Since the Israeli military operation on Nov. 4th, according to humanitarian groups, about 700 truck loads of goods have gone into Gaza. That's what should be going in-and-out on a single day.'</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-hamas_faq-141"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-hamas_faq_141-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://hamas.ps/en/page/13/FAQ" rel="nofollow"><i>Israel ended its occupation of the Gaza Strip when it withdrew from Gaza in 2005, so why does Hamas continue to fire rockets into Israel?</i></a>. Israel re-deployed its military occupation forces and evacuated its illegal settlers outside the population centers in Gaza. According to the UN and human rights organizations, Israel still maintains its occupation of the Gaza Strip and subjects the 1.8 million Palestinians in this tiny strip to a horrendous siege and blockade that constitute a war crime under international law." Here, Hamas cites the view of the international community.</span></li>
